(B) No person shall leave any unlicensed, uninsured or unregistered, or partially dismantled, or nonoperating, or wrecked or junked vehicle for a longer
time than forty eight (48) hours, on any street or right of way within the city.
(C) A vehicle that is registered, insured and operable may be considered abandoned if parked or stored on a street or legal right of way for a period
exceeding seventy two (72) hours.
Slight movement back and forth of the vehicle does not constitute a compliance with the seventy two (72) hours restriction.
(D) 1. Any reported vehicle violating this section shall first receive a warning notice of violation. Any vehicle not moved with twenty four (24) hours after
placement of the warning notice shall be cited for a parking infraction. Any vehicle not moved within seventy two (72) hours of receipt or placement of
theparking citation shall be towed at the direction of the police department.
2. The cost of removal and storage of the vehicle will be charged to the owner of the vehicle and/or the person causing the violation.
(E) No person in charge or control of any private property within the city whether as owner, tenant, occupant, lessee, or otherwise, shall allow more than
one unlicensed, or unregistered vehicle on any private property, unless the same is in an enclosed building, or is located on the premises of a business
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 55/151
enterprise operated in a lawful place and manner and provided said vehicles are necessary to the operation of such business enterprise.
(F) No person in charge or control of any private property within the city whether as owner, tenant, occupant, lessee, or otherwise, shall allow or leave any
partially dismantled, or nonoperating, or wrecked, or junked or discarded vehicle on private property within the city for a longer time than forty eight (48)
hours, except the same is in an enclosed building, or located on the premises of a commercial business enterprise operated in a lawful place and
manner, and provided said vehicles are necessary to the operation of such business enterprise.
(G) The term "vehicle" as used in this section is not to include recreational vehicles such as snow machines, motorcycles, golf carts, boats, campers and
motor homes unless these recreational vehicles are partially dismantled, or nonoperating, or wrecked, or junked, or discarded.
(H) No person in charge or control of any property within the city whether as owner, tenant, occupant, lessee, or otherwise shall allow any recreational
vehicles i.e., snow machines, motorcycles, golf carts, boats, campers and/or motor homes, to be parked upon any city street or city right of way during
the off season of said recreational vehicle.
"Off season" shall be defined to be the summer season for snow machines and the winter season for all other listed recreational vehicles.
1. "Winter season" shall further be defined as November 1 through March 1.
2. "Summer season" shall further be defined as March 2 through October 31.
(I) No person in charge or control of any property within the city whether as owner, tenant, occupant, lessee or otherwise, shall allow any utility trailer to
remain upon any city street or city right of way for more than forty eight (48) hours. (Ord. 569, 3-3-2004)
6-10-3: REMOVAL OF VEHICLES:
The police department of the city is hereby authorized in its discretion to see to the removal and subsequent handling of any vehicle found unlawfully on a
city street or right of way or private property within the city in accordance with the procedures set forth in chapter 18, title 49, Idaho Code, as presently
adopted or subsequently amended by the legislature of the state. (Ord. 569, 3-3-2004)
6-10-4: PRIMA FACIE RESPONSIBILITY FOR PARKING VIOLATION:
If a vehicle is stopped, standing, or parked in violation of this chapter, the person in whose name the vehicle is registered in this state or another state at
the time of the violation is prima facie responsible for that violation and subject to the fines and costs hereunder. (Ord. 569, 3-3-2004)
Chapter 11
OPERATION OF NONLICENSED MOTORIZED DEVICES
6-11-1: DEFINITIONS: As used in this chapter:
NONLICENSED MOTORIZED DEVICE: A steerable self-propelled vehicle with rubber tires, and shall specifically include golf carts and self-propelled lawn
mowers.
OPERATE: To control the operation of a nonlicensed motorized device.
OPERATOR: A person who operates or is in actual control of a nonlicensed motorized device.
PUBLIC STREET: Street, road, alleyway, or other public thoroughfare within the city limits. (Ord. 448, 9-19-1990)
6-11-2: PROHIBITED ACTS DESIGNATED:
(A) It is unlawful for any person to operate a nonlicensed motorized device within the city limits of the city under the following circumstances:
1. On private property of another without the express permission to do so by the owner or occupant of said property;
2. On public school grounds, park property, playgrounds, recreational areas and golf courses without express provision or permission to do so by the
proper public authority;
3. Within the right of way of any public street unless the operator has a valid driver's license issued by the state and has said driver's license in his
possession at the time of operating the device;
4. At a rate of speed in excess of fifteen (15) miles per hour;
5. Upon any public street, except as provided herein, said devices are not allowed to be on any portions of the followingpublic streets other than to
cross them in accordance with the provisions of subsection (A)8 of this section:
Fort Hall Avenue
Harrison Street
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 56/151
Idaho Street
Lincoln Street
Pocatello Avenue
Said devices will be permitted on all other public streets in the city, provided they otherwise comply with the provisions hereof, and provided they
operate said devices on the extreme right side of said roadways and as far as possible outside of the normal traveled area of the street;
6. Prior to one-half (1/2) hour after sunrise or later than one-half (1/2) hour before sunset;
7. Upon any public sidewalk or walkway;
8. Across any public street, except by a most direct route, this being at right angles to the side boundaries thereof;
9. With more than two (2) persons, including the operator, on said machine. (Ord. 448, 9-19-1990)
6-11-3: REQUIRED EQUIPMENT:
All nonlicensed motorized devices operated within the city shall have the following equipment:
(A) Manufacturer's stock grade mufflers, or equivalent, which are properly attached and which reduce the noise of operation of the vehicle within noise
level requirements of the laws of the state, and no person shall use a muffler cutout, bypass or similar device on said vehicle.
(B) Adequate brakes in good working order.
(C) A slow moving vehicle sign attached to the rear of said nonlicensed motorized device sized and located in accordance with applicable state law. (Ord.
448, 9-19-1990)
6-11-4: LEAVING UNATTENDED PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful for the owner or operator to leave or allow a nonlicensed motorized device to be or remain unattended on public property while the motor is
running or with keys for starting the vehicle left in the ignition. (Ord. 448, 9-19-1990)
6-11-5: YIELDING RIGHT OF WAY REQUIRED:
Nonlicensed motorized devices must yield right of way to allmotor vehicles licensed by the state for operation upon public highways, including, but not
limited to, the ingress and egress of the same to and from private property. (Ord. 448, 9-19-1990)
6-11-6: EXCEPTIONS FOR LAW ENFORCEMENT OFFICIALS:
The provisions hereof shall not apply to police officers in the performance of their duty. (Ord. 448, 9-19-1990)
6-11-7: FURTHER RESTRICTIONS AUTHORIZED:
The city council may, by resolution, further restrict or prohibit the operation of nonmotorized vehicles upon the public street or other public property within
the city and may restrict, extend, or change the public streets upon which nonlicensed motorized devices' operation may take place when, in their opinion,
the public safety and welfare so requires. (Ord. 448, 9-19-1990)
6-11-8: OBEDIENCE TO TRAFFIC REGULATIONS REQUIRED:
Each person operating a nonlicensed motorized device within the city shall strictly observe all traffic signs and signals and all other traffic rules and
regulations of the state, county, and/or city in addition to those rules and regulations set forth in this chapter and shall obey the orders and directions of any
peace officer authorized to direct or regulate traffic. (Ord. 448, 9-19-1990)
6-11-9: EXCEPTION FOR PARADES:
The provisions hereof shall not apply to the operation of said devices during any official police escorted parades in the city. (Ord. 448, 9-19-1990)
Title 7
FIRE REGULATIONS
Chapter 1
FIRE PREVENTION CODE
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 57/151
7-1-1: ADOPTION OF FIRE PREVENTION CODE:
For the purpose of regulating and governing conditions hazardous to life or property from fire, the several volumes of the national fire prevention codes
compiled and published by the National Fire Prevention Association together with such changes and amendments as may be hereafter published by the
association, are hereby adopted. Three (3) copies of said codes shall be kept on file at all times in the office of the clerk. (Ord. 363, 6-20-1979)
7-1-2: FLAMMABLE LIQUIDS:
The limits referred to in section 16.22a of the fire prevention code in which storage of flammable liquids in outside aboveground tanks is prohibited, are
hereby established as follows:
All residence zones. (Ord. 235, 9-1-1965)
Chapter 2
FIREWORKS
7-2-1: FIREWORKS DEFINED:
"Fireworks" shall include blank cartridges, toy pistols, toy cannons, toy canes or toy guns in which explosives are used, fire balloons, balloons of a type
which have burning material of any kind attached thereto or which require fire underneath to propel them, firecrackers, torpedoes, skyrockets, rockets,
Roman candles, fountain wheels, dago bombs, sparklers, and other fireworks of like construction and any fireworks containing any combustible or
explosive substances for the purpose of producing a visible or audible effect by combustion, deflagration, explosion or detonation.
Exempted from this section are all toy pistols, toy cannons, toy canes and toy guns and similar devices such as party poppers or party favors in which
paper caps containing not more than twenty five hundredths (0.25) grain of explosive compound per cap are used and such caps whether single, roll or
tape type and model rockets and model rocket engines designed, sold and used for the purpose of propelling of recoverable aero model rockets. (Ord.
251, 5-3-1967)
7-2-2: DANGEROUS FIREWORKS:
"Dangerous fireworks" include any of the following:
(A) Firecrackers, cannon crackers, giant crackers, salutes, silver type salutes, cherry bombs, mines, ground bombardment, grasshoppers and other
explosive articles of similar nature;
(B) Blank cartridges;
(C) Skyrockets and rockets, including all similar devices employing any combustible or explosive material and which rise in the air during discharge;
(D) Roman candles, including all devices which discharge balls of fire into the air;
(E) Chasers and whistles, including all devices which dart or travel about the surface of the ground during discharge;
(F) Snakes and hats containing bichloride of mercury;
(G) Sparklers more than ten inches (10") in length or one-fourth inch (1/4") in diameter or made with other than iron wires;
(H) All articles for pyrotechnic display such as aerial shells, salutes, flash shells, sky battles, parachute shells, wines, dago bombs and similar devices;
(I) All torpedoes which explode by means of friction, or which contain arsenic, and all other similar fireworks devices including cracker balls;
(J) Fire balloons or balloons of any type which have burning material of any kind attached thereto. (Ord. 251, 5-3-1967)
7-2-3: SAFE AND SANE FIREWORKS:
"Safe and sane fireworks" include any of the following:
(A) Cone fountains with pyrotechnic composition not exceeding fifty (50) grams each;
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 58/151
(B) Cylindrical fountains, whether base, spike or handle, with pyrotechnic composition not exceeding seventy five (75) grams each and inside tube
diameter not exceeding three-fourths inch (3/4");
(C) Sparklers and "dipped sticks" not more than ten inches (10") in length or one-fourth inch (1/4") in diameter made on steel or iron wire and Suziki and
morning glories with pyrotechnic composition not exceeding four (4) grams each;
(D) Snakes which do not contain bichloride of mercury and pyrotechnic composition not exceeding two (2) grams each;
(E) Wheels with pyrotechnic composition not exceeding sixty (60) grains for each driver unit or two hundred forty (240) grains for each complete wheel.
The inside tube diameter of drive unit shall not exceed one-half inch (1/2");
(F) Whistles, without report and which do not dart or travel about the ground during discharge with pyrotechnic compositionnot exceeding six (6) grams
and containing no picric or gallic acid. (Ord. 251, 5-3-1967)
7-2-4: DANGEROUS FIREWORKS PERMIT:
It shall be unlawful for any person in the city to import, export, offer for sale, sell, possess, keep or store or permit the keeping or storing of any "dangerous
fireworks" for any use or purpose, except that a person holding a dangerous fireworks permit issued pursuant to the terms and conditions of this chapter
may use "dangerous fireworks" for a safely supervised and conducted public display of fireworks. Said fireworks may be stored for a period not exceeding
ten (10) days immediately preceding the date of said public display, provided the fireworks are to be used exclusively for the public display. (Ord. 251, 5-3-
1967)
7-2-5: SAFE AND SANE FIREWORKS PERMIT:
No person without having a valid safe and sane fireworks permit issued pursuant to terms and conditions set forth in this chapter shall import, export,
possess for the purpose of sale, offer for sale, or sell any "safe and sane fireworks" for any use or purpose. (Ord. 251, 5-3-1967)
7-2-6: APPLICATION FOR SAFE AND SANE FIREWORKS PERMIT:
Any reputable person in reasonable pursuit or furtherance of any legitimate personal, business, or charitable purpose, desiring to engage in the sale of
"safe and sane fireworks" within the city shall first make written application to the clerk for a safe and sane fireworks permit. Each applicant shall pay to the
clerk a fee of ten dollars ($10.00) at the time he files his application. In the event no safe and sane fireworks permit is issued by the city by June 15 in the
year during which the application is made the clerk shall refund the application fee. At the time and as a condition of such filing, and with each application,
each applicant shall pay an additional fee to defray costs of preliminary investigations required hereunder and to be conducted by the said city, which fee
shall be eighteen dollars fifty cents ($18.50) per site applied for, and shall not be refundable in any event. (Ord. 251, 5-3-1967)
7-2-7: APPLICATION FOR DANGEROUS FIREWORKS PERMIT:
Any reputable person in reasonable pursuit or furtherance of any legitimate personal, business, or charitable purpose, desiring to make a public display of
"dangerous fireworks" shall first make written application to the clerk for a dangerous fireworks permit. Each applicant shall pay to the clerk a fee of ten
dollars ($10.00) at the time he files his application. In the event no dangerous fireworks permit is issued by the city by June15 in the year during which the
application is made, the clerk shall refund the application fee. At the time and as a condition of such filing, and with each application, each applicant shall
pay an additional fee to defray costs of preliminary investigations required hereunder and to be conducted by the said city, which fee shall be eighteen
dollars fifty cents ($18.50) per site applied for, and shall not be refundable in any event. (Ord. 251, 5-3-1967)
7-2-8: CONTENTS OF APPLICATION:
Each applicant for a safe and sane fireworks permit or a dangerous fireworks permit shall file his application with the clerk. Each application shall show the
following:
(A) Name and address of applicant.
(B) The purpose for which the applicant is primarily existing and for which it was organized.
(C) The names and addresses of the officers, trustees, and/or directors, if any, of the applicant.
(D) The location where the applicant requests permission to sell "safe and sane fireworks" or display "dangerous fireworks".
(E) When and where the applicant was organized and established, or, if a natural person, the applicant's age.
(F) The location of the applicant's principal and permanent meeting place or places, or principal place or places of business.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 59/151
(G) The applicant's state sales tax permit number.
(H) If the applicant is an entity other than a sole proprietorship, the name and general description of the business activities of each parent or subsidiary
company, business or entity, and a general description of the ownership organization of each person or subsidiary, if any.
(I) Such other information as the clerk may require on a standard form submitted to all applicants and which is reasonably necessary to protect the public
health, safety and morals. (Ord. 251, 5-3-1967)
7-2-9: INVESTIGATION:
The clerk shall cause an investigation to be made of each application and applicant and shall submit a written report of his findings and recommendations
for or against the issuance of the permit, together with his reasons therefor, to the council, which report shall not be public information except on request of
the applicant or by order of the council. (Ord. 251, 5-3-1967)
7-2-10: COUNCIL POWERS:
The council shall have the power in its discretion to grant or deny any application, subject to such reasonable conditions, if any, as it shall prescribe so
long as the denial of the application or any conditions imposed on the granting of the application are reasonably necessary for protection of the public
health, safety and morals. (Ord. 251, 5-3-1967)
7-2-11: VALIDITY; TERM:
A safe and sane fireworks permit, or a dangerous fireworks permit issued pursuant to this chapter shall be valid only within the calendar year in which
issued. A permit shall be valid only for the specific premises or location designated in the permit. However, subject to reasonable conditions necessary for
protection of the public health, safety and morals, an applicant may be granted permits for more than one premises or location within the city. No permit
shall be transferable or assignable. (Ord. 251, 5-3-1967)
7-2-12: APPLICATION TO BE FILED WITH CLERK:
Each application for a permit to sell "safe and sane fireworks" at retail shall be filed with the clerk on or before April 1, of the calendar year for which the
permit is sought; except that for the calendar year of 1967, applications for a permit may be filed on or before June 1, 1967. (Ord. 251, 5-3-1967)
7-2-13: LIABILITY INSURANCE REQUIRED:
Each applicant for a safe and sane fireworks permit or for a dangerous fireworks permit, shall have filed with the clerk prior to the issuance and validity of
any permit, a policy, or certified true copy thereof, of a public liability and products liability insurance, including both "accident" and "occurrence" coverage.
The insurance coverage limits for both public liability coverage and for products liability coverage shall be at least one hundred thousand dollars
($100,000.00) per person per occurrence, bodily injury three hundred thousand dollars ($300,000.00) per occurrence aggregate bodily injury, and one
hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) per occurrence aggregate property damage. Each policy of insurance shall be in form and substance acceptable
to the city, and shall name as insured parties under the terms of the policy the city, all officials, elected and appointed in performance of official functions
regarding all operations under or pertaining to said permit, any licensee or licensor of the applicant, and all vendors of the fireworks covered by the permit
to be issued to the applicant. Said policy of insurance shall be so written that it cannot be cancelled without at least ten (10) days' prior written notice to the
city from the underwriting insurance company. The dulylicensed insurance company or companies doing or authorized to do insurance business in Idaho,
and a copy of said policy shall be filed with the clerk prior to the issuance of the permit. (Ord. 251, 5-3-1967)
7-2-14: SALE PERIOD RESTRICTED:
No "safe and sane fireworks" shall be sold or offered for sale except from twelve o'clock (12:00) noon on June 26 to twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight on July
26 of each year. (Ord. 251, 5-3-1967)
7-2-15: TEMPORARY FIREWORKS STANDS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to offer for sale, sell, possess, keep or store, or permit the keeping or storing of any fireworks in any permanent building
or structure, nor in any other place within the city except in temporary fireworks stands as hereinafter described.
Temporary fireworks stands from which fireworks are to be sold shall be subject to the following provisions:
(A) All retail sales for fireworks shall be permitted only from within a temporary fireworks stand, and the sale from any other building or structure is hereby
prohibited.
(B) The stand in which the fireworks will be stored or sold shall not be located within twenty five feet (25') of any other building or within one hundred feet
(100') of any gasoline station or flammable liquid dispensing device or installation.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 60/151
(C) All such stands shall meet the requirements of the building code of the city and all lighting circuits and other electrical equipment shall meet the
requirements of the electrical code of the city.
(D) The stand shall have exit doors at least thirty inches (30") wide at both ends of the structure and one additional door for each twenty five feet (25') of
rear wall in excess of twenty five feet (25'). All doors shall open outward from the stand and all doorways shall be kept free and clear from all supplies
and materials at all times.
(E) Each stand shall be provided with a minimum of two (2) 21/2-gallon water type fire extinguishers, in good working order and easily accessible for use in
case of fire, which shall be kept in immediate proximity to the location where the fireworks are retailed.
(F) There shall be at least one supervisor, twenty one (21) years of age or older, on duty at all times. All fireworks shall be effectively kept away from any
kind of self-service by the public, and shall be placed in a location which is unavailableand inaccessible to members of the public in capacities other
than as legal customers. No person under eighteen (18) years of age shall work at or about any stand where fireworks are sold or offered for sale.
(G) No person employed as a watchman shall be permitted to remain inside of any stand when it is not open for business.
(H) "No Smoking" signs shall be prominently displayed both inside and outside the stands. No smoking shall be permitted within the stand or within twenty
five feet (25') of the stand.
(I) No temporary stand shall be erected before June 10 of any year. The premises on which the stand is erected shall be cleared of all structures and
debris, not later than twelve o'clock (12:00) noon of July 26.
(J) No fireworks shall be discharged in or within twenty five feet (25') of any fireworks stand.
(K) No person shall allow any rubbish to accumulate in or around any fireworks stand or permit a fire nuisance to exist.
(L) No fireworks shall remain unattended at any time regardless of whether the fireworks stand is open for business or not. If any fireworks are stored, they
shall only be stored at such places as are approved for storage of fireworks by the city fire chief or his representative.
(M) No stand shall have a floor area in excess of seven hundred fifty (750) square feet. (Ord. 251, 5-3-1967)
7-2-16: RECORDS TO BE KEPT:
Each permittee shall be required to retain at the licensed premises while said premises are open, and at the principal place of business for a year
thereafter, copies of all invoices, receipts and orders evidencing the source from which he acquired the fireworks which he handled. (Ord. 251, 5-3-1967)
7-2-17: BOND OR DEPOSIT:
In those cases where the applicant conducts the sale of fireworks from a temporary fireworks stand, he shall post with the clerk a cash bond or cash
deposit in the amount of not less than fifty dollars ($50.00) or such other security as may be acceptable to the mayor or council conditioned upon the
prompt removal of the temporary fireworks stand and the cleaning up of debris from the site of the temporary fireworks stand, which deposit or security
shall be returned to the applicant only in the event he removes said temporary fireworks stand and cleans up all debris to the satisfaction of the city fire
chief, or such other official as the council or fire chief may designate. In the event of the applicant's failure to remove the stand and the debris, said
cashbond or cash deposit shall be forfeited to the city. In no event shall the applicant be entitled to the return of said cash bond or cash deposit if he has
failed to remove said temporary fireworks stand and clean up all debris by twelve o'clock (12:00) noon of July 26 of any year. It shall be the legal duty of
each permittee to clear such sites and remove all debris therefrom on or before July 26 of the year in which the permit is granted, and failure to do so shall
be punishable by a two hundred fifty dollar ($250.00) fine and/or thirty (30) days' confinement in the city jail. (Ord. 251, 5-3-1967)
7-2-18: COMPLIANCE; VIOLATION:
It shall be the duty of every person issued a fireworks permit to comply with all the provisions of the Idaho state fireworks act and this chapter. The
conviction of violation of the aforesaid Idaho state fireworks act or any of the provisions of this chapter by the permittee, or any of its agents, employees, or
officers shall constitute a cause, in and of itself, to deny any subsequent application for a permit. (Ord. 251, 5-3-1967)
Chapter 3
EXPLOSIVES
7-3-1: EXPLOSIVES PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to make, keep or transport any gunpowder, nitroglycerin or other highly explosive substance within the limits of the city.
(1960 Code)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 61/151
7-3-2: EXCEPTION PERMITTED:
A vehicle carrying explosives may be permitted on the streets of the city only if a special written permit has first been obtained from the chief of police;
such permit shall specify the exact route to be used by said vehicle and may permit the vehicle to be parked at a certain specified place for a certain
specified amount of time. Each such permit shall be valid only for the one specified use. (1960 Code)
Title 8
PUBLIC SERVICES
Chapter 1
PUBLIC SERVICES GENERAL REGULATIONS
8-1-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this title is to:
(A) Establish reasonable rules and regulations for the operation of the water, sewer, and sanitation departments of the city.
(B) Establish reasonable fees to be charged to customers receiving water, sewer or sanitation service and provide fair, orderly and efficient procedures for
collection and termination of delinquent accounts.
(C) Establish a fair and equitable means of having persons who hook into and receive a direct and immediate benefit from existing water and sewer mains
by requiring them to participate in the capital cost of water mains fronting upon their property and which have been constructed from revenues derived
from the operation of the water and sewer systems.
(D) Establish a fair and equitable charge for the actual cost of materials and labor expended by the city whenever the city crews install water service for a
customer.
(E) Protect the public health and welfare by controlling cross connections or other sources or potential sources of contamination to the city water supply; to
prevent the introduction of pollutants into the American Falls wastewater system which will interfere with the normal operation of the system or
contaminate the resulting sludge; to prevent the introduction of pollutants into the American Falls wastewatersystem which do not receive adequate
treatment in the publicly owned treatment works (POTW) and which will pass throughout the system into receiving waters or the atmosphere or
otherwise be incompatible with the system.
(F) Provide a clean, efficient and adequate water system; sewer collection and treatment system; and garbage collection system for the residents of the
city. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-1-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this title, the terms, phrases, words, and their derivations shall have the meanings given herein. When not inconsistent with the context,
words used in the present tense include the future, words in the plural number include the singular number, and words in the singular number include the
plural. The word "shall" is always mandatory and not merely directory. The following definitions apply to all sections of this title:
AUTHORITY: The city of American Falls.
CITY: The mayor and city council of the city of American Falls, Idaho.
CITY CODE: As defined in section 1-1-1 of this code.
CITY INSPECTOR: The person designated by the city.
CITY STANDARDS: The Idaho standards for public works construction, as amended, unless otherwise indicated by the city.
EASEMENT: An acquired legal right for the specific use of land owned by others.
MAY: Is permissive (see definition of Shall).
OWNER: A person owning real estate which is, or proposes to be, connected to the water or wastewater system, or using the garbage collection system.
PWD: Public works director.
PERSON: Any individual, firm, company, association, society, corporation or group.
PURVEYOR: The city of American Falls or its authorized agent.
SHALL: Is mandatory (see definition of May).
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 62/151
USER: A person using the water; wastewater; or garbage collection system. This is synonymous with "owner". (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-1-3: SYSTEM MANAGEMENT GENERALLY:
The rules and regulations set forth in this chapter are established for the management of the municipal water system; the municipal sewer collection;
wastewater treatment system; and the garbage and refuse collection system of the city. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-1-4: PUBLIC WORKS DIRECTOR:
The public works director shall oversee and superintend the planning, operation and maintenance of the municipal water system; the municipal sewer
collection; wastewater treatment system; and the garbage and refuse collection system of the city, the making of repairs of all kinds, the construction of all
extensions and additions and all construction work of whatever nature whatsoever in connection with the present water system; sewer collection system;
wastewater treatment facility; and the garbage and refuse collection system; and any new system that may be established.
The public works director shall be subject at all times to the direction and authority of the city council. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-1-5: RECORD KEEPING AND FUNDS:
The city clerk-treasurer shall collect and receive all monies payable, pursuant to law, by patrons of the city water, sewer, and garbage departments. The
city clerk-treasurer shall keep full and complete records of all such monies received, the date and from whom received and shall also keep accurate and
complete account of all disbursements showing the date and amount thereof, the person to whom paid, and upon what account. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-1-6: SERVICE APPLICATIONS:
All applications for water, sewer, and garbage service shall be made at city hall, and shall be made by the owner of the property to be served, or by his
duly authorized agent.
When water and sewer service connections have been installed, application for water and sewer service shall be made either by the owner, or his duly
authorized agent. If the property to be served is a rental, the owner may have the billing submitted in the renter's name by completing an owner's consent
form. This form authorizes the billing to be sent to the renter, but notifies the owner that he is still responsible for nonpayment of the billing.
The city shall turn on or shut off the water services only at the request of the owner of the property, or owner's agent asdesignated in writing by the owner.
(Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-1-7: DIGGING PERMIT REQUIRED:
No person shall dig or excavate in any street or alley or under the sidewalk for the purpose of laying, removing, or repairing any water or sewer line, or for
any other purpose, without first obtaining a permit.
As a prerequisite to the issuing of such permit, the city clerk-treasurer, after notice to the building department, street department and sewer department,
shall require a fee in an amount to be set by the city council and a refundable fee, bond or undertaking from the applicant in such form as required by the
city council, which said refundable fee, bond or undertaking shall be to guarantee that the street or alley be returned to its former condition within a
reasonable time after the digging or excavation permitted by the permit.
The deposit will be refunded by the city clerk upon inspection and approval by the street superintendent. (Ord. 581, 8-16-2006)
8-1-8: WATER, SEWER, GARBAGE COLLECTION RATES:
The schedule of rates, fees and charges for water, sewer, and garbage collection shall be set from time to time by resolution of the city council. Copies of
all resolutions subsequently passed by the city council pursuant to this section shall be kept on file and made available in the office of the city clerktreasurer.
(Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-1-9: BILLING PROCEDURES:
(A) All services shall be billed on a monthly basis. The billing period for water, sewer and garbage collection service shall extend from the first to the last
day of each calendar month. Services will be billed in advance and no deposit will be required. Water, sewer, and garbage collection bills shall be
combined and billed monthly. The bill becomes past due on the sixteenth day of the calendar month in which it was issued.
(B) For purposes of this section, "owner" shall mean any person or entity who holds legal or equitable title to the property. For purposes of this section,
"occupant" shall mean a person or entity who is physically in possession of the property and is legally responsible for the upkeep and maintenance of
the same, including, but not limited to, the head of any extended family residing thereon.
(C) The owner of each building connected to the water supply of the city and/or the sewage collection system or utilizingthe garbage collection system of
the city shall be responsible and legally liable for the payment of all water, sewer, and garbage collection charges assessed.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 63/151
(D) Pursuant to arrangements with the owner, a tenant of said owner may pay such charges and reduce the owner's liability by the amount of any such
payment. Acceptance by the city of such payment from a tenant shall not constitute a waiver by the city of the owner's liability for any charges not paid
by the tenant.
(E) If a building has more than one residential tenant or business utilizing space in the building, then the owner of the building shall be responsible and
legally liable for the payment of the total utility charges for all tenants in the building. The charge to be levied upon the owner shall be computed as
follows: the base fee for the building shall be the fee established for the heaviest water user tenant located in the building. For each additional tenant
without separate water service the owner shall be billed one-half (1/2) of the minimum water rate established for that type of business. If a tenant has a
separate water service, the owner will be billed the full amount established for that type of business. Sewer service fees and garbage collection fees
shall be as set by resolution.
(F) Multi-units shall be billed in full each month with credit memos given for vacancies only if the amount due is paid in full by the end of the current month.
(G) A full billing will be charged for water, sewer and garbage collection services unless the water is shut off at the city valve by city personnel only. If the
water is turned on, the owner shall not have the option to be exempt from the garbage collection service fee regardless of whether or not the owner is
utilizing the service. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-1-10: WHEN PAYABLE:
Bills shall be due and payable on the date mailed and shall be deemed delinquent if not paid within fifteen (15) days following the mailing date. Water or
sewer or garbage collection service, any or all, shall be discontinued if payments are more than thirty (30) days' delinquent. A delinquency charge in an
amount to be established by resolution shall be added to each delinquent bill for each certified mailing or personal service provided to said user, to defray
the costs of the city in sending out such notices.
A fee shall also be assessed for all returned checks given to the city for payment of bills as established by resolution.
Upon disconnection of either a water or sewer connection for nonpayment of bills, a reconnection charge shall be assessed in an amount to be established
by resolution. (Ord. 515,1-7-1998)
8-1-11: NOTICE OF DELINQUENCIES AND HEARING PROCEDURES:
If the bill has not been fully paid by the fifteenth day of the month after which it was issued, the same shall become delinquent and a written notice of the
delinquency and impending termination of water service shall be mailed to the premises. The written notice shall be served or mailed at least seven (7)
days prior to suspending service. Such notice shall state the date on which service is to be suspended and the right to request in writing a pretermination
hearing. This hearing will be held before the city council, who shall have the power to review disputed bills and rectify errors in the billing; provided said
written request is received by the city clerk-treasurer at least one day prior to the proposed suspension date.
Upon receipt of such timely request, the city council shall give written notice to the party requesting the hearing as to the date, time and place of said
hearing, which hearing will be held not sooner than five (5) days from the date of the request.
The city council shall make a record of any pretermination hearing and shall, within ten (10) days of the hearing, render a decision in writing, giving
reasons for the determination. (Ord. 551, 12-6-2000)
8-1-12: TERMINATION OF SERVICE:
If a request for a pretermination hearing is not made within ten (10) days after the written notice provided for herein is mailed to the premises, or if an
adverse decision is rendered against the party requesting the hearing, the city shall immediately thereafter suspend water, garbage collection and sewer
service, unless satisfactory payment arrangements are made. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-1-13: RESTORATION OF SERVICE:
In the event that water, garbage collection, and sewer service has been terminated, the same shall be restored only upon the payment of any past due
amounts still owing upon the utility bill, plus a reconnection charge for water and sewer service. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-1-14: TURNON FEES FOR WATER SERVICE:
Except for the reconnection charge, provided for in section 8-1-13 of this chapter, there shall be no turn on/off fee for water service where arrangements
are made to have serviceturned on or off during the regular workweek (Monday through Friday) between eight o'clock (8:00) A.M. and five o'clock (5:00)
P.M., except for legal holidays.
In the event water service is turned on or off at any other time at the property owner's request, or in the cases of an emergency due to broken water lines,
etc., there shall be imposed, in addition to other fees required by this title and chapter, an after hours service charge, as established by resolution. (Ord.
515, 1-7-1998)
8-1-15: PAYMENT OF PAST DUE ACCOUNTS:
At the time of application for water, sewer, or garbage collection service, or of application for restoration of the same, and prior to the commencement or
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 64/151
restoration of such service, the owner or occupant of any lot, property, building or residence for which such service is requested shall pay to the city any
and all past due amounts for water, sewer, or garbage collection service to the city, by such owner or occupant, whether such past due amounts are
attributable to the property for which service is now sought or are attributable to other property in the city currently or previously owned or occupied by the
applicant. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-1-16: WATER TURNOFF OR TURNON RESTRICTIONS:
Any water connection valve may be turned off for nonpayment of service or at any such time that an authorized city representative determines that a
health or safety hazard exists. The service will remain off until payment is made in full or the hazard is remedied by the property owner.
The city reserves the right, at any time, without notice, to shut off the water supply for repairs, extensions, or in other cases of necessity; and the city shall
not be responsible for any damage such as bursting of boilers supplied by direct pressure, the breaking of any pipes or fixtures, stoppage or interruption of
water supply, or any other damage resulting from the shutting off of water.
(A) It shall be unlawful for any person, entity, association, partnership, corporation, or other legal entity to turn "on" or "off" or otherwise tamper with any
city water connection valve that has been turned off by city officials.
(B) It shall also be unlawful for any person to accept the benefit of availability of city water service that has been previously turned off by the city.
(C) At any time any city water connection valve is turned off, for nonpayment or any other code violation, a written "notice of turnoff" shall be affixed to the
curb stand. Said noticeshall also set out the provisions hereof relative to criminal sanctions for violations thereof. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-1-17: VIOLATIONS AND PENALTIES:
Any person who violates, disobeys, omits, neglects, refuses to comply with, or resists the enforcement of any of the provisions of this title, or the rules and
regulations as adopted by the purveyor, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall for each offense be punished by a
fine, or imprisonment, or by both such fine and imprisonment as established by title 1, chapter 3 of this code. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
Chapter 2
MUNICIPAL WATER SYSTEM
8-2-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to set forth uniform requirements for users of the American Falls water system and to enable the city to protect public health
in conformity with all applicable state and federal laws pertaining thereto. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-2-2: DEFINITIONS:
All general definitions1 shall apply to this chapter along with the following definitions which are specific to the water system:
BACKFLOW/BACK SIPHONAGE: The flow other than in the intended direction of flow, of any nonpotable waters, foreign liquids, gases or harmful or
offensive substances into the city water supply as a result of reduced or reversed pressure.
BACKFLOW PREVENTION DEVICE: A device which, when properly installed between the city water supply system and the terminus of the customer's
water line or point of ultimate use, will prevent backflow/back siphonage.
CONTAMINATION: The entry into or presence in a public water supply of any substance which may be deleterious to health and/or quality of water.
CORPORATION STOP: The valve located on city main to which service line connects.
CROSS CONNECTION: Any physical arrangement whereby a public water supply is connected, directly or indirectly, with any other water supply system,
sewer, drain, conduit, pool, storage reservoir, plumbing fixture or other device which contains or may contain contaminated water, sewage or other waste
or liquids of unknown or unsafe quality which may be capable of introducing contamination to the public water supply as a result of backflow.
CURB STOP: The valve on the water service line, owned by the city and located near the customer's property line.
CUSTOMER LINE: The pipe, valves and fittings leading from the curb stop into the premises served, including the water meter (if applicable) attached
thereto.
METER: A water meter and its enclosure, valve and related appurtenances.
METER BOX: The enclosure in which the water meter is installed, located at or near the property line.
PUBLIC WATER SUPPLY: Any system or water supply intended or used for human consumption or other domestic uses, including source, treatment,
storage, transmission, distribution facilities, where water is furnished to any collection or number of individuals, or is made available to the public for human
consumption or domestic use.
VALVE BOX: The enclosure that fits over a buried valve through which a turn key fits that allows the valve to be operated.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 65/151
WATER MAIN: The publicly owned water pipe laid in a street, road, alley or easement.
WATER SERVICE LINE: The water pipe, valves and fittings laid from the main to the curb stop. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-2-3: SEPARATE WATER CONNECTION REQUIRED:
(A) It shall be unlawful for any residential or commercial unit to be constructed or placed upon a lot within the city from and after the date hereof that does
not have its own separate water connection.
(B) Each property capable of title transfer and each residence located on any one property shall be considered as an individual consumer, and each
individual consumer shall besupplied through a separate service connection; provided, however, that in case of duplexes or apartments not being
capable of separate title transfer, the owner thereof may, nevertheless, by arrangement with the water department, provide for said property multiple
service connections, to serve each of the various apartments located thereon.
(C) All buildings, although joined together by party wall or similar attachments, if capable of separate title transfer, shall have for each divisible part thereof,
separate service connections.
(D) Where water through one service is furnished to two (2) or more residences or buildings occupied by different families on acreage property capable of
subdivision and transfer by proper title in fee simple, the plumbing thereon shall be arranged so that each divisible part thereof shall have its own
separate service connection.
(E) No new connection of residential or commercial units or buildings will be permitted onto the city water system until this requirement is met. (Ord. 515,
1-7-1998)
8-2-4: WATER SERVICE LINE INSTALLATION AND CHARGES:
Within a platted subdivision, a private contractor hired by the customer shall install the water service line between the main line and the curb stop, valve
box and meter box, subject to acceptance by the city as required by the American Falls development code2.
All other water service lines between the main line and the curb stop shall be installed by the city.
Whenever a water service line is installed by the city, the charges for labor and materials shall be established and modified from time to time by resolution
of the city council and shall be paid by the owner of the property. The water service line installation fee shall include the cost of pipe desired and general
conditions of the installation plus fifteen percent (15%) for overhead charges. Charges for the costs for boring, blasting or unusual rock removal shall also
be added to the charge to the customer. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-2-5: WATER MAIN CONSTRUCTION FEE:
This section establishes an equitable system of charging new customers for the impact or burden created whenever they enlarge an existing water service
or connect a new water service to the existing wells, storage tanks, pumps, outbuildings, and appurtenances of the city water system, allof which were
funded from revenues of the city water system. The city recognizes the inherent inequity of requiring existing customers to bear the entire cost of acquiring
or building new facilities, or of utilizing excess capacity with existing facilities, in order to meet the needs of such new development.
The council hereby finds and recognizes the relationship between the nature of the uses of property and the impact thereof upon the city water system.
The council also finds that customers who connect to a water main located adjacent to their property receive a direct benefit from such water mains, which
benefit is directly proportional to the frontage of the water main along their property. The council further finds that it is fair and equitable to charge a main
construction fee for customers who connect to such mains in order to fund a portion of the cost incurred by the city in installing such mains. (Ord. 515, 1-7-
1998)
8-2-6: WATER MAIN CONSTRUCTION CHARGES:
(A) All persons desiring to connect to any water main which is constructed, following the effective date of this title, in whole or in part, at city expense shall
pay a water main construction fee. This fee shall be established and modified from time to time by resolution of the city council.
(B) The charges shall be calculated on a per front foot basis of property owned by such person(s) and fronting upon a street or public right of way within
which a water main is located. Such fee shall be in addition to the water service line installation fee set forth above, and does not include the costs, if
any, for boring, blasting or unusual rock removal in construction of the main. The necessary and reasonable costs for such services shall be added to
the per front foot cost.
(C) If any such property is located upon a corner or is bounded by two (2) or more streets in which a water main is located, the calculations for the fee shall
be based upon the frontage of the longest street in which water main is located.
(D) All water mains within the city shall be deemed to have been constructed in whole or in part at city expense, unless the applicant presents written
evidence conclusively demonstrating that such main was constructed entirely from private monies or was constructed entirely with funds from a state or
federal grant.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 66/151
(E) This water main construction charge shall not apply to extensions of mains undertaken by the city for its own purposes where there is no pending
request for extension, such as when the city needs to make a loop in its system. Extensions are subject to available funding, and nothing herein shall
be construed to require the city to construct an extension to the system.
(F) However, the city may, in its discretion, grant permission to a developer to construct a water main entirely at his or her expense. In that event, the city
may, by written agreement, pay over to the developer all water main construction fees collected by the city from any other person who subsequently
connects to such water main within five (5) years completion of the main. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-2-7: INSTALLATION AND MAINTENANCE:
All water mains and service lines shall be installed and maintained by the city. The city shall also maintain those private installations accepted by the city.
(Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-2-8: PERMITS AND SERVICE CONNECTION FEES:
It shall be unlawful to install, alter, or connect any water service maintained by the city without obtaining a permit from the city and paying the service line
connection fee and, if applicable, the water main construction fee. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-2-9: EXTENSION OF WATER MAINS OUTSIDE CITY:
Water mains shall not, without the approval of the city council, be extended outside the corporate limits of the city, and unless adequate excess water is
available for such service. Such agreements shall specifically reserve the right to terminate such service without cause, at any time, upon at least thirty
(30) days' advance written notice, or as otherwise negotiated between the city and the owner of the property. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-2-10: BRANCH SERVICE:
No service connection serving more than one customer shall be made. Where an existing water service provides service to several customers, the city
may terminate water service until a separate service is provided at the owner's expense. If the city does not terminate service to these existing services,
the established rate shall be charged for each customer receiving service from the existing line. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-2-11: INCREASING SIZE OF EXISTING RESIDENTIAL OR COMMERCIAL SERVICE LINE:
The size of an existing residential or commercial service line may be increased at the request of the owner of the property. The cost of increasing the line
shall be based on the existing fee established by resolution. This will be considered a newhookup and charged accordingly. The owner of the property will
need to abandon the smaller line or pay the utility billing in full for two (2) services. The city, not the property owner, shall disconnect the smaller line if
requested. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-2-12: DESIGN AND CONSTRUCTION OF WATER MAIN EXTENSIONS:
All design plans and specifications for the construction of public water mains shall be prepared and approved by a professional engineer, registered in the
state of Idaho, and approved by the state of Idaho department of environmental quality. All construction of water main extensions shall also conform to the
approved plans and specifications as established by the current issue of the Idaho standards for public works construction, this code, and the standards
established by the city, and shall be approved by the public works director before the city assumes any responsibility for the maintenance of the water line.
The owner or the owner's contractor shall notify the PWD one day before any excavation is begun. No trench backfill shall be placed until the city has
inspected and approved the water pipe and a city inspector is available to inspect and test the backfill material. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-2-13: ABANDONED SERVICE:
All service installations connected to the water system that have been abandoned or that have not been used for two (2) years or that for any reason have
become useless for further service, at the discretion of the city, shall be disconnected at the main by the water department, and all pipe and appurtenances
removed shall be the property of the city. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-2-14: RESPONSIBILITY FOR FROZEN PIPES AND LEAKS:
All service installations, except summer sprinkling services, shall be placed at the depth required to avoid all probability of freezing, and the water
department shall be responsible for all frozen services owned by the city, and the owners of property served shall be responsible for all other frozen
services leading to and located on the premises served, and shall pay the cost of thawing of such privately owned pipes whenever necessary.
Owners of services are responsible for all leaks or damages on account of leaks from privately owned services and privately owned water lines leading
from the property line to the premises served. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-2-15: WASTING WATER PROHIBITED:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 67/151
It is unlawful for any person to waste water or allow it to be wasted by imperfect or leaking stops, valves, pipes, closets, faucets or other fixtures, or to use
toilets without self-closing valves, or unattended open hoses; or to use water in violation of this chapter regulating use of water. The wilful wasting of water
is a misdemeanor; if such waste of water continues after receiving notice from the water department to make repairs and to desist from the waste of water,
the water department shall shut off the water supply from such premises until the necessary repairs have been made. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-2-16: METERS:
The PWD has the option to require the installation of water meters on any existing or new water system connections. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-2-17: CROSS CONNECTION:
No water service connection to any premises shall be installed or continued in use by the purveyor unless the water supply is protected by backflow
prevention devices as may be required by this chapter. The installation or maintenance of a cross connection which will endanger the water quality of the
potable water supply of the city shall be unlawful and is prohibited. Any such cross connection now existing or hereafter installed is hereby declared to be
a public nuisance and the same shall be abated. The control or elimination of cross connections shall be in accordance with this chapter together with the
latest edition of appropriate manuals of standard practice pertaining to the cross connection control approved by the state. The PWD shall have the
authority to establish requirements more stringent than state regulations if he deems that conditions so dictate. The purveyor shall adopt rules and
regulations as necessary to carry out the provisions of this chapter. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-2-18: USE OF BACKFLOW PREVENTION DEVICES:
(A) Backflow prevention devices shall be installed at the tees on the premises or with service connection or within any premises where, in the judgment of
the purveyor, the nature and extent of the activities, or materials stored on the premises, would present an immediate, or potential, dangerous hazard
to health and/or be deleterious to the quality of water should a cross connection occur, even though such cross connection does not exist at the time
the backflow prevention devices shall be installed under circumstances including, but not limited to, the following:
1. Premises having an auxiliary water supply.
2. Premises having internal cross connections that are not correctable, or intricate plumbing arrangements that make it impractical to ascertain whether
or not cross connections exist.
3. Premises where entry is restricted so that inspections for cross connections cannot be made with sufficient frequency or at sufficiently short notice to
assure that cross connections do not exist.
4. Premises having a repeated history of cross connections being established or reestablished.
5. Premises on which any substance is handled under pressure so as to permit entry into the public water supply, or where a cross connection could
reasonably be expected to occur. This shall include the handling of process waters and cooling waters.
6. Premises where materials of a toxic or hazardous nature are handled in such a way that if back siphonage should occur, a serious hazard might
result.
7. The following types of facilities will fall into the above categories and a backflow prevention device is required to protect the public water supply. A
backflow prevention device shall be installed at these facilities:
(a) Hospitals, mortuaries, clinics.
(b) Laboratories.
(c) Metal plating industries.
(d) Sewage treatment plants.
(e) Food or beverage processing plants.
(f) Chemical plants using a water process.
(g) Petroleum processing or storage plants.
(h) Radioactive material processing plants or nuclear reactors.
(i) Others specified by state.
8. Other premises, as specified by the PWD, where backflow prevention devices are required to protect the public water supply.
(B) The type of protective device required shall depend on the degree of hazard which exists:
1. An air gap separation or a reduced pressure principle backflow prevention device shall be installed where the public water supply may be
contaminated with sewage, industrial waste of a toxic nature, or other contaminant which could cause a health or system hazard.
2. In the case of a substance which may be objectionable, but not hazardous to health, a double check valve assembly, air gap separation or a reduced
pressure principle backflow prevention device shall be installed.
(C) Backflow prevention devices required by this chapter shall be installed at the meter, at the property line of the premises when meters are not used or at
a location designated by the purveyor. The device shall be located so as to be readily accessible for maintenance and testing, and furthermore, where
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 68/151
no part of the device will be submerged.
(D) Backflow prevention devices required by this chapter shall be installed under the supervision of and with the approval of the purveyor.
(E) Any protective device required by this chapter shall be a model approved by the PWD. A double check valve assembly or a reduced pressure principle
backflow prevention device will be approved if it has successfully passed performance tests of the state or other testing laboratories satisfactory to the
state and the PWD. These devices shall be furnished and installed by and at the expense of the customer.
(F) Backflow prevention devices installed pursuant to this chapter, except atmospheric vacuum breakers, shall be inspected and tested upon installation
and annually, or more often if necessary. Inspections, tests and maintenance shall be at the customer's expense. Whenever the devices are found to
be defective, they shall be repaired or overhauled or replaced at the customer's expense. Inspections, tests, repairs and records thereof shall be
accomplished under the purveyor's supervision by state certified testers.
(G) No underground sprinkling device will be installed without adequate backflow prevention devices at the point from which the water for irrigation is taken
from the public water supply. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-2-19: INSTALLATION PERMITS:
If cross connection control device(s) is found to be necessary, the owner of the property served must apply to the city for a specific installation permit. No
cross connection control device may be installed, removed or relocated without a valid permit. A permit fee shall be established by resolution. (Ord. 515, 1-
7-1998)
8-2-20: ADDITIONAL REMEDIES:
In the event an improper cross connection is not corrected within the time limit set by the PWD, or, in the event the purveyor is refused access to any
property for the purpose of determining whether or not cross connections exist, delivery of water to the property shall cease until the deficiency is corrected
to the purveyor's satisfaction. In addition, the purveyor may effect the necessary repairs or modifications at the expense of the property owner and refuse
delivery of water to the property until the cost thereof shall have been paid. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
Chapter 3
MUNICIPAL WASTEWATER COLLECTION AND TREATMENT SYSTEM
8-3-1: PURPOSE:
To set forth the uniform requirements for dischargers into the city's wastewater collection and treatment systems and enabling the "authority", the city, to
protect public health in conformity with all applicable state and federal laws pertaining thereto. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
All general definitions1 shall apply to this chapter along with the following definitions which are specific to the wastewater collection and treatment system:
ASTM: American Society for Testing Material.
APPLICABLE PRETREATMENT STANDARDS: For any specified pollutant, city prohibitive discharge standards, city's specific limitations on discharge, the
state of Idaho pretreatment standards or the national categorical pretreatment standards (when effective), whichever standard is most stringent, or
whichever is in effect at the time of issuance of an industrial water acceptance form.
BIOCHEMICAL OXYGEN DEMAND (BOD): The quantity of oxygen utilized in the biochemical oxidation of organic matter under standard laboratory
procedure in five (5) days at twenty degrees centigrade (20C), expressed in milligrams per liter.
BUILDING DRAIN: That part of the lowest horizontal piping of a discharge system which receives the discharge from soil, waste and other drainage pipes
inside the walls of the building and conveys it to the building sewer, beginning five feet (5') (1.5 m) outside the inner face of the building wall.
BUILDING SEWER: The extension from the building drain to the public sewer or other place of disposal, also called "house connection".
CATEGORICAL PRETREATMENT STANDARDS: The national pretreatment standards specifying quantities, concentrations of pollutants or pollutant
properties which may be discharged or introduced into the POTW by specific industrial dischargers.
COOLING WATER: The water discharged from any use, such as air conditioning, heat exchangers, cooling or refrigeration or to which the only pollutant
added is heat.
DISCHARGER; INDUSTRIAL DISCHARGER: Any nonresidential user who discharges an effluent into a POTW by means of pipes, conduits, pumping
stations, force mains, constructed drainage ditches, surface water intercepting ditches, intercepting ditches and all constructed devices and appliances
appurtenant thereto.
FLOATABLE OIL: Oil, fat or grease in a physical state such that it will separate by gravity from wastewater by treatment in an approved pretreatment
facility. Wastewater shall be considered free of floatable fat if it is properly pretreated and the wastewater does not interfere with the collection system.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 69/151
FLOW (Q): The volume of wastewater being discharged into the wastewater system.
GARBAGE: The animal and vegetable waste resulting from the handling, preparation, cooking and serving of foods.
ISPWC: Idaho standards for public works construction.
IWA: Industrial wastewater acceptance form.
INDUSTRIAL USER: Any user discharging nondomestic wastes into the sewerage system.
INDUSTRIAL WASTES: Solid, liquid, or gaseous waste resulting from any industrial, manufacturing, trade, or business process or from the development,
recovery, or processing of natural resources.
INTERFERENCE: An inhibition or disruption of the POTW, its treatment processes or operations, or its sludge processes, use of which is a cause of or
significantly contributes to either a violation of any requirement of the POTW's NPDES permit (including an increase in the magnitude or duration of a
violation) or to the prevention of sewage sludge use or disposal by the POTW in accordance with the following statutory provisions and regulations or
permits issued thereunder (or more stringent state or local regulations): section 405 of the clean water act, the solid waste disposal act (SWDA) (including
title 11, more commonly referred to as the resource conservation and recovery act [RCRA] and including state regulations contained in any state sludge
management plan prepared pursuant to subtitle D of the SWDA), the clean air act, and the toxic substances control act. An industrial user significantly
contributes to such a permit violation or prevention of sludge use or disposal in accordance with the above cited authorities whenever such user:
(A) Discharges a daily pollutant loading in excess of that allowed by contract with the POTW or by federal, state or local law;
(B) Discharges wastewater which substantially differs in nature or constituents from the user's average discharge; or
(C) Knows or has reason to know that its discharge, alone or in conjunction with discharges from other sources, would result in a POTW permit
violation or prevent sewage sludge use or disposal in accordance with the above cited authorities as they apply to POTW's selected method of
sludge management.
NPDES: The national pollutant discharge elimination system permit program as administered by the USEPA or state.
NATURAL OUTLET: Any outlet, including storm sewer overflows, into a watercourse, pond, ditch, lake or other body of surface or ground water.
NEW SOURCE: Any building, structure, facility or installation from which there is or may be a discharge, the construction of which commenced: a) after
promulgation of pretreatment standards2 under section 307(c) of the act which are applicable to such source; or b) after proposal ofpretreatment standards
in accordance with section 307(c) of the act which are applicable to such sources, but only if the standards are promulgated in accordance with section
307(c) within one hundred twenty (120) days of their proposal.
POTW: Publicly owned treatment works. Any sewage treatment works and the sewers and conveyance appurtenances discharging thereto, owned and
operated by the authority.
pH: The logarithm of the reciprocal of the hydrogen ion concentration. The concentration is the weight of hydrogen ions in grams per liter of solution.
Neutral water, for example, has a pH value of seven (7) and hydrogen ion concentration of 10-7.
POLLUTANT: Any substance discharged into a POTW or its collection system, as described within section 8-3-6 of this chapter and/or listed in appendices
A and B, section 8-3-25 of this chapter.
PRETREATMENT: The reduction of the amount of pollutants, the elimination of pollutants, or the alteration of the nature of pollutant properties in
wastewater to a less harmful state prior to or in lieu of discharging or otherwise introducing such pollutants into a POTW.
PROPERLY SHREDDED GARBAGE: The wastes from the preparation, cooking and dispensing of foods that have been shredded to such a degree that
all particles will be carried freely under the flow conditions normally prevailing in a public sewer, with no particle greater than one-half inch (1/2") (1.27 cm)
in any dimension.
SANITARY SEWER: A sewer that carries liquid and water carried wastes from residences, commercial buildings, industrial plants and institutions, together
with minor quantities of ground water, that are not admitted intentionally.
SERVICE SADDLE: A gasketed band that fits around the outside of the sewer main into which the service line is installed.
SEWER: A pipe, conduit, ditch or other device used to collect and transport wastewater and storm water from the generating source.
SIGNIFICANT INDUSTRIAL DISCHARGER (SID): Any industrial user of the city's wastewater disposal system who:
(A) Is subject to or potentially subject to national pretreatment standards promulgated under section 307(b) or (c) of the clean water act (CWA); or
(B) Has in their wastes any priority toxic pollutants listed in appendix A, section 8-3-25 of this chapter or other toxic pollutantslisted in appendix B,
section 8-3-25 of this chapter; or
(C) Has in their wastes toxic pollutants as defined pursuant to section 307 of the CWA; or
(D) Has a discharge flow of twenty five thousand (25,000) gallons or more per average workday; or
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 70/151
(E) Has an average workday flow greater than five percent (5%) of the daily average flow for the previous month flow in the city's wastewater treatment
system; or
(F) Is determined by the city to have a significant impact or potential for significant impact, either singularly or in combination with other contributing
industries, on the wastewater treatment system, the quality of sludge, the system's effluent quality, or air emissions generated by the system.
SLUG LOAD: Any discharge of water or wastewater which, in concentration of any given constituent or in any quantity of flow, exceeds for any period of
duration longer than fifteen (15) minutes more than five (5) times the average twenty four (24) hour concentration of flows during normal operation, or
which adversely affects the collection system or causes interference to the POTW.
STORM DRAIN: A drain or sewer for conveying water, ground water, subsurface water or unpolluted water from any source.
TOTAL SUSPENDED SOLIDS (TSS): Total suspended matter that either floats on the surface of or is in suspension in water, wastewater or other liquids
and that is removable by laboratory filtering as prescribed in "standard methods for the examination of water and wastewater" and referred to as
nonfilterable residue.
TOXIC POLLUTANTS: Those substances listed in appendix A, section 8-3-25 of this chapter "Priority Pollutants", and any other pollutant or combination of
pollutants listed as toxic in regulations promulgated by the administrator of the environmental protection agency under section 307 of the clean water act.
UPSET: Any exceptional incident in which a discharger unintentionally and temporarily is in a state of noncompliance with the standards set forth in
appendices A and B, section 8-3-25 of this chapter due to factors beyond the reasonable control of the discharger, and excluding noncompliance to the
extent caused by operational error, improperly designed treatment facilities, inadequate treatment facilities, lack of preventive maintenance, or careless or
improper operationthereof.
WEF: Water environment federation.
WASTEWATER: The spent water of the community. From the standpoint of source, it may be a combination of the liquid and water carrying wastes from
residences, commercial buildings, industrial firms and institutions, together with minor quantities of ground water, surface water and storm water that may
be discharged into the POTW.
WASTEWATER COLLECTION SYSTEM: A collective term referring to the entire piping system that transports wastewater from its source to the city
wastewater treatment plant.
WASTEWATER SYSTEM: A collective term referring to all facilities necessary to collect wastewater from the users and treat it prior to discharge into the
Snake River.
WASTEWATER TREATMENT OPERATOR: The person appointed by the city to be responsible for the operation and maintenance of the POTW under the
direction of the PWD.
WASTEWATER TREATMENT SYSTEM: A collective term referring to the apparatus used to treat polluted wastewater after it leaves the collection system.
WATERCOURSE: A natural or artificial channel for the passage of water either continuously or intermittently. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-3: PROHIBITED ACTS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to do any of the following:
(A) To place, deposit or permit to be deposited in any unsanitary manner on public or private property within the city or any area under the jurisdiction of
said city, any human or animal excrement, garbage, objectionable waste or other matter detrimental to health.
(B) To discharge into any natural outlet within the city, or in any area under the jurisdiction of said city, any wastewater or other polluted waters, except
where suitable treatment has been provided in accordance with subsequent provisions of this chapter.
(C) To construct or maintain any privy, privy vault, septic tank, cesspool, or other private wastewater disposal facility intended or used for the disposal of
wastewater or to connect to or use the city wastewater collection system, except as hereinafter provided.
(D) To maliciously, wilfully and negligently break, damage,destroy, uncover, deface or tamper with any structure, appurtenance or equipment which is a
part of the wastewater facilities. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-4: USE OF PUBLIC SEWERS REQUIRED:
(A) All houses, buildings or properties under the jurisdiction of the city used for human occupancy, employment, recreation or other purposes that contain
facilities designed to discharge wastewater shall connect such facilities to a public or private wastewater disposal facility conforming to the provisions
contained herein, and no permit to construct a building shall be issued until evidence has been submitted to the building administrator that the owner
has obtained a permit, as provided herein, to construct a private wastewater disposal facility or to connect to a public sewer for the purpose of
wastewater disposal.
(B) Each owner, tenant, or occupant of each lot or parcel of land in the city upon which a building shall have been constructed for residential, commercial,
or industrial use, within three hundred feet (300') (92 m) of a street or other public way which now contains or shall hereafter contain a sanitary sewer
shall connect such building with the sewage collection system of the city and shall cease to use any other method for the disposal of sanitary or
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 71/151
industrial sewage. No exceptions to this requirement shall be made except by council action. All such connections shall be made in accordance with
the rules and regulations to be adopted from time to time by the council.
(C) Upon annexation, the owner of all existing houses, buildings, or properties served by a private wastewater disposal system shall, at the owner's
expense, abandon the private wastewater disposal system and make any necessary line extensions and connect to and discharge all wastewater into
a public sewer as provided herein, at any time a public sewer becomes available for extension and/or connection, without the need for a lift station,
within three hundred feet (300') (92 m) of the property line. The abandonment of the private facility and connection to the public facility shall be
completed within sixty (60) days after the state department of health and welfare or the city PWD notifies the owner, in writing, of the availability of a
public sewer of the city, or that the private facility is not functioning properly and is causing a health problem. In the event that a lift station is required,
the owner may negotiate with the city to connect to the public sewer.
(D) The developer of a new subdivision shall, at his expense, construct the necessary extensions of the public sewer system to provide public sewer
facilities for each lot in the subdivision.
(E) Upon failure of any lot or parcel of real estate to beconnected to the sewage collection system within thirty (30) days after such connection is required
under the foregoing provisions hereof, the city shall send, by first class mail, a notice to the owner shown on the last available tax assessment roll and
