the lessee or other occupant of each building so required to be connected declaring that failure to make connection within ten (10) days from the date
notice is mailed will result in disciplinary action.
(F) If any required connection is not made within the period described by such notice, the city shall take one or more of the following steps:
1. Shut off water service.
2. Make the required connection and assess the cost thereof, with penalty, against the real estate involved and commence proceedings against the
owners of such real estate involved.
(G) Every owner or lessee or other occupant of any building which is required to be connected to the sewage collection system of the city shall, after the
expiration of the period mentioned in the notice prescribed by subsection (E) of this section, cease to use any other manner of disposing of sanitary or
industrial sewage. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-5: CONNECTION TO PUBLIC SEWER, PROCEDURE:
Any owner of property outside the corporate limits of the city who desires to connect to a public sewer shall first obtain approval of the city council and
upon such approval shall sign a contract for providing sewer service. Approval by the city council shall be based on the availability of surplus capacity in
the public facility and its determination that the connection will not have a detrimental effect on the health, safety or welfare of the other users of the
wastewater system. The contract for providing sewer service shall, as a minimum, contain an agreement to comply with all policies, rules and regulations
governing the wastewater system and to pay all fees and charges for services provided, all as established herein. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-6: GENERAL DISCHARGE PROHIBITIONS:
(A) No person shall connect any possible source of inflow to the sewer collection system of the city unless the source of inflow is from a residential,
commercial, or industrial use approved by the city. It shall be illegal to connect any sump pumps, foundation drains, storm drains, surface runoff drains
or other drainage by surface means to the city sewage collection system. No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any natural drainage
waters such as storm water, ground water, roof runoff or subsurface drainage to any public sewer. Such natural drainage water shall be discharged
tosewers that are specifically designated as storm sewers or to a natural outlet approved by the PWD and other regulatory agencies. Natural drainage
water from limited areas which is polluted at times may be discharged to the wastewater collection if such discharge is approved by the PWD and such
fee as may be established by the city council is paid. Cooling waters or process waters shall be discharged to the public sewer; except that discharge
to a storm sewer or natural outlet shall be required if the water is never polluted based upon approval of the PWD and the appropriate state and federal
pollution control agencies.
(B) No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any of the following described substances into the wastewater disposal system or otherwise to
the facilities of the authority:
1. Any liquids, solids, or gases which by reason of their nature or quantity are, or may be, sufficient either alone or by interaction with other substances
to cause fire or explosion hazard, or be injurious in any other way to the POTW or to the operation of the POTW. At no time shall two (2) successive
readings on any explosion hazard meter, at the point of discharge into the system (or at any point in the system), be more than five percent (5%) nor
any single reading over ten percent (10%) of the lower explosive limit (LEL) of the meter. Prohibited materials include, but are not limited to, gasoline,
kerosene, naphtha, benzene, toluene, xylene, ethers, alcohols, ketones, aldehydes, peroxides, chlorates, perchlorates, bromates, carbides,
hydrides, sulfides, and any other substances which the authority, the state or USEPA has notified the user is a fire hazard or hazard to the system.
2. Any toxic or poisonous solids, liquids or gases in sufficient quantity, either singly or by interaction with other wastes, to injure or interfere with any
waste treatment process, constitute a hazard to humans or animals, create a public nuisance, prevent entry into the collection system for
maintenance and repair or create any hazard in the receiving waters.
3. Any waters or wastewater having a pH lower than 6.5 or higher than 9 or having any other corrosive property capable of causing damage or hazard
to structures, equipment and personnel of the wastewater works, or capable of interfering with any wastewater treatment process.
4. Solid or viscous substances capable of causing obstructions to the flow in sewers, or other interference with the proper operation of the wastewater
facilities such as, but not limited to, ashes, bones, cinders, sand, mud, spent lime, stone or marble dust, grass clippings, spent grains, spent hops,
wastepaper, asphalt residues, residues from refining or processing of fuel or lubricating oil, or glass grinding or polishing wastes, straw, shavings,
metal, glass, rags, feathers, tar, plastics, wood, underground garbage, wholeblood, paunch manure, animal hides, hair and fleshings, entrails and
paper dishes, cups, milk containers, disposable diapers, etc., either whole or ground by garbage grinders.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 72/151
5. Wastewater or process water having a temperature higher than one hundred fifty degrees Fahrenheit (150F) or sixty five degrees Celsius (65C).
6. Any wastewater having a temperature which will inhibit biological activity in the POTW treatment plant resulting in interference; but in no case,
wastewater with a temperature at the introduction into the POTW treatment plant which exceeds forty degrees Celsius (40C) or one hundred four
degrees Fahrenheit (104F) unless the POTW treatment plant is designed to accommodate such temperature.
7. Wastewater containing more than twenty five milligrams per liter (25 mg/l) of petroleum oils, nonbiodegradable cutting oils or product of mineral oil
origin.
8. Wastewater containing floatable oils, fat or grease.
9. Any garbage that has not been properly shredded as defined in section 8-3-2 of this chapter.
10. Wastewater containing toxic pollutants in sufficient quantity either singly or by interaction to injure or interfere with any wastewater treatment
process, constitute a hazard to humans or animals, or to exceed the limitations set forth in the categorical pretreatment standards. A toxic pollutant
shall include, but not be limited to, any pollutant identified in the toxic pollutant list set forth in appendix A, section 8-3-25 of this chapter, "Priority
Pollutants".
11. Any waters or wastes containing odor producing substances exceeding limits established by the authority.
12. Any radioactive wastes or isotopes of such half life or concentration as may exceed limits established by the authority in compliance with applicable
state or federal regulations.
13. Quantities of flow, concentrations, or both, which constitute a "slug load" as defined in section 8-3-2 of this chapter.
14. Waters or wastes containing substances which are not amenable to treatment or reduction by the wastewater treatment processes employed, or
are amenable to treatment only to such degree that the wastewater treatment plant effluent cannot meet the requirements of other agencies having
jurisdiction over discharge to the receiving waters.
15. Any waters or waste which may: interact with other waters or wastes in the public sewer system; release obnoxious gases; form total suspended
solids which interfere with thecollection system; or create a condition deleterious to structures and treatment processes.
16. Any substance which may cause the city's sewage treatment plant effluent or any other product of the city's sewage treatment plant such as
treatment residues, sludges, or scums to be unsuitable for reclamation and reuse or to interfere with the reclamation process. In no case shall a
substance be discharged to the sewage system which may cause the city to be in noncompliance with sludge use or disposal criteria, guidelines, or
regulations affecting sludge use or disposal developed pursuant to the solid waste disposal act, the clean air act, the toxic substance control act, or
state criteria applicable to the sludge management methods being used.
17. Any substance which will cause the POTW to violate its NPDES and/or other disposal system permits.
18. Any substance or objectionable color not removed in the treatment process, such as, but not limited to, dye wastes and vegetable tanning
solutions.
19. Any wastewater from septic tanks, except if they are discharged at the location authorized by the PWD.
20. Any water or waste containing fats, wax, grease or oils, whether emulsified or not, in excess of one hundred milligrams per liter (100 mg/l) or
containing substances which may solidify or become viscous at temperatures between thirty two degrees Fahrenheit (32F) or zero degrees
centigrade (0C) and one hundred fifty degrees Fahrenheit (150F) or sixty five degrees centigrade (65C).
21. Pollutants released in such strength or volume as to cause interference in the treatment plant. The following discharges are not permitted unless
approved otherwise in writing by the PWD:
(a) A standard five (5) days biochemical oxygen demand (BOD) greater than three hundred (300) parts per million by weight; or
(b) Wastes containing more than three hundred fifty (350) parts per million by weight of total suspended solids; or
(c) Wastes containing any quantity of substances that this title declares may not be discharged into any public sewer; or
(d) A chlorine concentration of more than twenty milligrams per liter (20 mg/l); or
(e) An average daily flow greater than two percent (2%) of the average daily flow carried by the treatment facility receiving the waste; or
(f) Wastewater at a flow rate and/or pollutant discharge ratewhich is excessive over a relatively short time period so that there is a treatment process
upset and subsequent loss of treatment efficiency.
(C) Substances, materials, waters or wastes are considered objectionable discharges into a wastewater system if, due to their concentration, quantity or
other characteristics, they are harmful to the sanitary sewers, wastewater treatment plant or they have an adverse effect on the treatment or receiving
stream or they will endanger lives, limb or public property or they constitute a nuisance. Such discharges may be limited in concentration or quantity or
otherwise restricted or may be required to be treated before discharge into a public sewer. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-7: LIMITATIONS ON WASTEWATER STRENGTH:
Wastes shall not be discharged into the city sewer system unless the limitations, restrictions or other requirements outlined by current state, local or
federal, whichever are more stringent, have been complied with. The following limitations shall apply to wastewater discharged into the city's sewerage
system:
(A) Current national categorical pretreatment standards as promulgated by the U.S. environmental protection agency (USEPA) pursuant to the act shall be
met by all dischargers of the regulated industrial categories. An application for modification of the national categorical pretreatment standards may be
considered for submittal to the regional administrator by the authority, when the authority's wastewater treatment system achieves consistent removal
of the pollutants as defined by CFR part 403.7.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 73/151
(B) State requirements and limitations on dischargers to the POTW shall be met by all dischargers which are subject to such standards in any instance in
which they are more stringent than federal requirements and limitations or those in this chapter or any other applicable ordinance.
(C) No discharger shall increase the use of potable or process water in any way for the purpose of diluting a discharge as a partial or complete substitute
for adequate treatment to achieve compliance with the standards set forth in this chapter.
(D) In addition to the previously stated discharge limits, no discharger shall discharge wastewater exceeding concentrations or the materials listed in
appendix B, section 8-3-25 of this chapter. The authority may impose mass limitations on dischargers which are using dilution to meet the pretreatment
standards or requirements of this chapter, or in other cases where the imposition of mass limitations is deemed appropriate by the authority.
(E) The authority reserves the right to amend this chapter to provide for more stringent limitations or requirements on discharges to the POTW where
deemed necessary to comply with the objectives set forth in this chapter. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-8: SPECIAL AGREEMENTS:
No statement contained in this chapter shall be construed as preventing any special agreement or arrangement between the city and any industrial user
whereby an industrial waste of unusual strength or character may be accepted by the city for treatment, except that no agreement will relieve the industrial
user of obligation under pretreatment regulations 40 CFR part 4.03 or any promulgated categorical pretreatment standards. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-9: ACCIDENTAL DISCHARGES:
(A) Each discharger shall provide protection from accidental discharge of prohibited or regulated materials or substances established by this chapter.
Where necessary, facilities to prevent accidental discharge of prohibited materials shall be provided and maintained at the discharger's cost and
expense. Detailed plans showing facilities and operating procedures to provide this protection shall be submitted to the authority for review, and shall
be approved by the authority before construction of the facility. Each existing significant industrial discharger shall complete and submit same to
authority within one hundred eighty (180) days from the effective date hereof or within ninety (90) days from issuance of an industrial wastewater
acceptance form, whichever is sooner.
(B) Dischargers shall notify the authority immediately upon the occurrence of a "slug load" or accidental discharge of substance prohibited by this chapter.
The notification shall include location of discharge, date and time thereof, type of waste, concentration and volume and corrective actions. Any
discharger who discharges slugs of prohibited materials shall be liable for any expense, loss, or damage to the POTW, in addition to the amount of any
fines imposed on the authority on account thereof under state or federal law. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-10: USE OF PUBLIC SEWER:
(A) Any industrial user covered by individual wastewater discharge contracts with the city are still subject to the requirements of this chapter. When any
waters or wastes discharged or proposed to be discharged to the public sewer will constitute an objectionable discharge as defined above, or will
require more than available capacity of the wastewater treatment plant or collection system or will otherwise createa harmful effect on the economic,
social or environmental welfare of the community, the city council may:
1. Reject the wastewater;
2. Require pretreatment of wastewater to an acceptable condition before discharge to the public sewers;
3. Require facilities to equalize waste flows by controlling the quantities and rates of discharge of wastewater; and/or
4. Require extra payment to cover added cost of handling and treating the wastewater not covered by existing sewer charges.
When considering the above alternatives, the city council shall give consideration to the economic impact of each alternative on the discharger. If the
city council permits the pretreatment or equalization of waste flows, the design and installation of the plant and equipment shall be subject to the
review and approval of the PWD. Where pretreatment or flow equalizing facilities are provided or required for any waters or wastes, they shall be
maintained continuously in satisfactory and effective operation by the owner at their expense.
(B) When, in the opinion of the PWD, grease, oil and sand interceptors are necessary for the proper handling of objectionable discharges containing
floatable grease in excessive amounts, or any flammable wastes, sand or other harmful ingredients, such interceptors shall be provided and
maintained by the owner. All interceptors shall be of a type capacity and design approved by the PWD and shall meet all requirements of the uniform
plumbing code and shall be located so as to be readily and easily accessible for cleaning and inspection. In the maintaining of these interceptors the
owner shall be responsible for the proper removal and disposal of the captured material and shall maintain records of the dates and means of disposal
which are subject to review by the PWD. The means of removing and disposing of captured material shall be subject to approval of the PWD and must
be performed according to the state statutes governing such removal and disposal. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-11: PRIVATE WASTEWATER DISPOSAL:
(A) When connection to a public wastewater facility is not required, as provided herein, then the owner may construct and maintain at their expense a
private wastewater disposal facility in accordance with this section.
(B) Before commencement of construction of a private wastewater disposal system, the owner shall obtain a permit from the Idaho department of health
and welfare. The application for such permit shall be made through the Idaho department of health and welfare and the applicant shallfurnish any
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 74/151
plans, specifications and other information as are deemed necessary by said department.
(C) A permit for a private wastewater disposal system shall not become effective until the installation is completed to the satisfaction of the Idaho
department of health and welfare. The department's representative shall be allowed to inspect the work at any stage of construction and, in any event,
the applicant for the permit shall notify the department when the work is ready for final inspection and before any underground portions are covered.
(D) The type, capacity, location and layout of private wastewater disposal system shall comply with all recommendations of the Idaho department of health
and welfare. No discharge to any natural outlet will be allowed from any private wastewater disposal system.
(E) The owner shall operate and maintain the private wastewater disposal facilities in a sanitary manner at all times, at no expense to the city. Disposal of
sludge from private wastewater disposal systems will be performed by a currently licensed waste disposal firm (if such license is required at that time)
and will be deposited at the county landfill or at such other location outside the city limits as may be approved by the county commissioners. Sludge
from private wastewater disposal systems shall not be deposited in the city wastewater collection system except at such locations as may be approved
by the PWD and at such fee as may be established by the city council.
(F) Whenever a private wastewater disposal system is abandoned, all sludge shall be removed and properly disposed of and the tank shall be filled with
soil, all to the satisfaction of the PWD.
(G) No statement contained in this section shall be construed to interfere with or supersede any additional requirements that may be imposed by the Idaho
department of health and welfare. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-12: BUILDING SEWERS AND SERVICE CONNECTIONS:
No person shall install or alter any sanitary sewer within the city, or tap into or connect to any sanitary sewer line, whether lateral, main or interceptor,
without first obtaining a permit from the city.
(A) No person except authorized city employees shall uncover, make any connections with or openings into, use, alter or disturb any public sewer or
appurtenance thereof without first obtaining a written permit from the PWD.
(B) There shall be three (3) classes of sewer service connection permits:
General permit for residential, residential-commercial, noncommercial or commercial users;
Industrial permits for industrial users; and
Municipal permits for other municipalities using the system.
1. General Permits: General permits shall be classified as in city and out of city permits:
(a) In City General Permits: In city general permits shall be applied for by the owner or the owner's agent on a form provided by the city clerktreasurer.
In city general permits shall be approved by the PWD. Approval shall only be contingent upon the availability of a public sewer adjacent
to the owner's property and the applicable provisions of this title.
(b) Out Of City General Permits: Out of city general permits shall be applied for by the owner on a form provided by the city clerk-treasurer and shall
be accompanied by an executed copy of the standard agreement for services outside the city limits. Out of city general permits shall be
accompanied by an executed copy of the standard agreement for services outside the city limits. Out of city general permits shall be approved by
the city council based on recommendation by the PWD. Approval shall be contingent upon the availability of a public sewer adjacent to the owner's
property, execution of the agreement for services outside the city limits and conformance of the proposed land use with city comprehensive plan
and the applicable provisions of this title.
2. Industrial Permits: Industrial permits shall be applied for by the owner or the owner's agent by letter to the city council accompanied by an executed
copy of the standard industrial user agreement together with any plans, specifications or other information considered pertinent by the PWD, and/or
city council. Industrial permits shall be approved by the city council based on recommendation by the PWD. Approval shall be contingent upon the
same criteria used for general permits, the availability of excess capacity in the wastewater system, the applicable provisions of this title and any
other considerations the city council deems appropriate.
3. Municipal Permits: Municipal permits shall be applied for by the municipality by letter to the city council accompanied by any information considered
pertinent by the PWD and/or city council. Municipal permits shall be approved by the city council based on recommendation by the PWD. Approval
shall be contingent upon any considerations the city council deems appropriate.
(C) Service connections shall include the tap into the public sewer and the sewer service line between the tap and theprivate use area. The property owner
or the owner's agent shall be authorized to tap into the sewer collection main designated by the city after obtaining appropriate permits. The city will
supply the service saddle necessary to connect into the public sewer main.
(D) No trench backfill shall be placed until the service connection is inspected and approved by the city. The owner shall be responsible for notifying the
PWD when a connection is ready for inspection.
(E) All work in public trafficways is subject to approval by the PWD and shall be done in accordance with city code regulations and according to standards
established by the PWD. The owner or owner's agent shall notify the PWD one day before any excavation is begun and must have obtained an
excavation permit as required by title 9, chapter 10 of this code.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 75/151
Any connection so made must be of proper design and of the appropriate materials as established by the city that are in effect at the time of the
connection.
(F) A separate and independent building sewer and service connection shall be provided for every building; except, where one building stands at the rear
of another on an interior lot and no public sewer is available or can be constructed to the rear building through an adjoining alley, court, yard or
driveway, the city may allow the front building sewer to be extended to the rear building and the whole considered as one building sewer, but the city
does not and will not assume any obligation or responsibility for damage caused by or resulting from any such single connection aforementioned.
(G) Old building sewers may be used in connection with new buildings only when they are found, on examination and test by the PWD, to meet all
requirements of this chapter.
(H) The size, slope, alignment, materials of construction of a building sewer and the methods to be used in excavating, placing of the pipe, connection into
the public sewer, jointing, testing and backfilling the trench shall all conform to the requirements of the uniform building and uniform plumbing codes or
other applicable rules and regulations of the city. In the absence of code provisions or in amplification thereof, the materials and procedures set forth in
appropriate specifications of the ASTM and the WPCF manual of practice no. 9 shall apply.
(I) Whenever possible, the building sewer shall be brought to the building at an elevation below the basement floor. In all buildings in which any building
drain is too low to permit gravity flow to the public sewer, sanitary sewage carried by such building drain shall be lifted by an approved means and
discharged to the building sewer.
(J) No person shall make connection of roof downspouts,foundation drains, areaway drains or other sources of surface runoff or ground water to a building
sewer or building drain which in turn is connected directly or indirectly to a public sanitary sewer, unless such connection is approved by the PWD for
purposes of disposal of polluted surface drainage. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-13: SEWER CONNECTION FEES REQUIRED:
Before any permit is issued for the installation or alteration of any sanitary sewer, or before any connection is made to any sanitary sewer line, whether
lateral, main or interceptor, the applicant shall pay to the city a sewer connection fee, which fees may hereafter be established and modified from time to
time by resolution of the city council. A separate sewer connection permit must be obtained for each building using the sanitary sewer system of the city,
and except as otherwise provided herein, the service connection fee must be paid whenever a permit is required by the city.
Once the required sewer service connection fee has been paid for any building connected to the sewage collection system of the city, no further
connection fee shall be charged for the connection of any sewer serving any building constructed or reconstructed at the same place, or so near the same
place that no substantial extension of the original side sewer is necessary to serve it. However, if a new tap to the city sewer main is requested or required,
an inspection fee will be charged and a sewer service saddle will be installed. The city shall provide and be reimbursed for the actual cost of the sewer
service saddle. Proof of payment of the fee or proof of location of existing line shall be furnished by the applicant, and in the absence of such proof, a
connection fee shall be charged. (Ord. 520, 5-6-1998)
8-3-14: SEWER MAIN CONSTRUCTION CHARGE:
All persons desiring such connection to any sewer main which is constructed, following the effective date hereof, in whole or in part at city expense, shall
pay a sewer main construction charge to be established and modified from time to time by resolution of the city council.
(A) The charges shall be calculated on a per front foot basis of property owned by such person and fronting upon a street or public right of way within
which a sewer main is located. Such fee shall be in addition to the sewer system connection fee set forth in section 8-3-13 of this chapter.
(B) If any such property is located upon a corner or is bounded by two (2) or more public rights of way in which a sewer line is located, the calculation for
the sewer main construction fee shall be based upon the frontage of the longest public right of way in which a sewer main is located.
(C) All sewer mains within the city shall be deemed to have been constructed in whole or in part at city expense, unless the applicant presents written
evidence conclusively demonstrating such main was constructed entirely with funds from a state or federal grant.
(D) This sewer main construction charge shall not apply to extensions of mains undertaken by the city for its own purposes where there is no pending
request for extension.
(E) Extensions are subject to available funding, and nothing herein shall be construed to require the city to construct an extension to the system. However,
the city may, in its discretion, grant permission to a developer to construct a sewer main entirely at his or her expense. In that event, the city may, by
written agreement, pay over to the developer all sewer main construction fees collected by the city from any other person who subsequently connects
to such sewer main within five (5) years of completion of the main. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-15: DESIGN AND CONSTRUCTION OF PUBLIC SEWERS:
If a developer is granted permission to construct a sewer main entirely at his or her expense, the following design and construction requirements shall be
met:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 76/151
(A) All design plans and specifications for the construction of public sewers shall be prepared and approved by a professional engineer registered in the
state of Idaho and approved by the state of Idaho department of environmental quality. All plans and specifications shall conform to standards
established by the city and shall be approved by the city and the PWD prior to construction of any public sewer.
(B) All public sewers shall be constructed in a public utility easement, trafficway or other approved right of way, properly dedicated to the public, which is
not less than fifteen feet (15') in width.
(C) The developer shall be responsible for the cost of design and construction of new public sewers in accordance with the policies established by
resolution of the city council for the "engineering and construction of improvements within public rights of way and easements within the jurisdiction of
the city and the payment of same" and in accordance with any special agreements required by the city council and for the cost of design and
construction of any existing public sewers in accordance with the provisions of this code governing sewers constructed by private funds or sewers
constructed by public funds.
(D) Construction of public sewers shall conform to the approved plans and specifications, this code and the standards established by the city, the current
issue of ISPWC and shallbe approved by the PWD before the city assumes any responsibility for the maintenance of the sewer. The owner or the
owner's contractor shall notify the PWD one day before any excavation is begun. No trench backfill shall be placed until the city has inspected and
approved the sewer pipe and a city inspector is available to inspect and test the backfill material. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-16: SEWER CONNECTION FEES ESTABLISHED:
Sewer connection fees shall be established by resolution of the city council. The fees so established shall be sufficient to reimburse the city for all
connections costs. Each fee shall be a fixed amount representing the average cost incurred for performing the service for which reimbursement is sought.
The following fees shall be established:
(A) General Permit: Reimbursement for processing applications and inspections for a general permit.
(B) Industrial Permit: Reimbursement for processing applications and inspections for an industrial permit.
(C) Municipal Permit: Reimbursement for processing applications and inspections for a municipal permit. This fee shall be established by the city council
on an individual basis based on the actual cost.
(D) Reimbursement; Standard Connection: Reimbursement for constructing a standard sewer connection four inches (4"), six inches (6"), or eight inches
(8") in diameter.
(E) Reimbursement; Nonstandard Connection: Reimbursement for a larger than standard diameter building sewer. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-17: USER CHARGES:
(A) General user charges shall be established by resolution of the city council. Industrial user charges and municipal user charges shall be established by
separate agreement with the city council. All charges so established shall be in proportion to the benefits derived by the user from the wastewater
service and shall be in accordance with U.S. government regulations. The charges so established shall generate sufficient revenue to repay all bonded
indebtedness, to repay the U.S. government for all loans made to local industrial users, to operate and maintain the wastewater facilities and to build a
reserve fund sufficient to pay for the future capital improvements to the wastewater facilities. The total revenue required for the wastewater system
shall be collected from all users by equitably proportioning the cost to each user based on the amount of flow (Q), biochemical oxygen demand (BOD)
and total suspended solids (TSS) the useris contributing to the total system.
(B) Since measuring the individual Q, BOD and TSS contributed by each user and collecting his proportionate share of the total cost based on unit
charges for each characteristic is impractical, the general users shall be grouped in classes having similar characteristics, and the average Q, BOD and
TSS contributed by the class shall be used to determine the proportionate share of the total cost that should be generated by the class. The revenue to
be generated by the class shall then be divided by the total flow contributed by the class to establish a unit cost per one thousand (1,000) gallons of
wastewater discharged or by the total number of users in a class to establish a unit cost per user. The user charge paid by each user shall reasonably
approximate the proportional share the user would pay if the user's individual Q, BOD and TSS contribution were measured and the user's share were
calculated using the same unit charges for each characteristic that was used to determine the proportionate share of the total cost that should be
generated by each user class.
(C) The city council shall establish user classes, the charge to be levied against each user in a class and the distribution of revenues from each class. The
PWD shall place each user in a class so established and calculate his charge for wastewater service. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-18: SCHEDULE OF RATES:
(A) Sewer User Classification And Rate Schedule:
1. It is hereby declared to be the policy of the city that all rates for sewage service within the city and without the boundaries of the city shall be
reasonable and just and shall take into account and consideration the cost and value of the system and the operation and maintenance expenses of
the system, including repairs, debt repayment, replacement costs, depreciation, and other direct and indirect obligations incurred on behalf of said
system which are to be charged against all users of the service at such rates and amounts as shall be sufficient to secure the required revenues
necessary to meet the aforementioned expenses. No free service shall be provided to the city or any other user on the system; provided, further, that
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 77/151
no discrimination shall be made in the rates to be charged other than that required due to the type or volume of waste generated as hereinafter
provided.
2. Any equitable user classification and assessment formula must assess each customer class with their pro rata portion of the volume strength loading
of that class.
3. Said user assessment must also assess against each customer class, a surcharge equal to any above normal strength wastewater loading.
4. Based on sample flow studies made by the city, the current average flow per residence in the city equals an estimated two hundred (200) gallons of
wastewater flow per day per thirty (30) day average month for a total estimated average residential volume loading per month of six thousand (6,000)
gallons.
5. Based upon sample analysis of the biochemical oxygen demand (BOD) and total suspended solids (TSS) of said residential loading, the estimated
normal strength of said residential loading for which the plant is designed will contain not more than one hundred eighty milligrams per liter (180 mg/l)
of biochemical oxygen demand (BOD) and one hundred eighty milligrams per liter (180 mg/l) of total suspended solids.
6. Using said residential loading as a base rate and using existing flow data for flow loading from representatives of each customer class within the city
for plant loading from all other sources, the following user classification and user rate schedule is hereby adopted.
The base sewer rate as established by resolution shall be multiplied by the equivalent user as specified below to determine the monthly rate to be
charged:
User Classification
Equivalent Users
(Each)

1.1 Single-family 1.00
1.2 Multiple-family unit 1.00
1.3 Manufactured home spaces 1.00

2.1 Schools 6.50
2.2 Churches 1.00

Note:
1.Rates for all industrial users will be determined by flow sampling as to volume generated, and strength and type of waste involved.
7. Prior to any industrial user being allowed to hook into the city wastewater facilities, a prior agreement with the city and said proposed user as to the
estimated volume and nature of discharge from said user into the city treatment plant will be established and the rate set in accordance with the
formula set out therein.
8. For purposes of user rate formula calculation, "normal strength waste" will be defined as waste having a total suspended solids (TSS) strength of not
more than one hundred eighty milligrams per liter (180 mg/l) and a biochemical oxygen demand (BOD) of not more than one hundred eighty
milligrams per liter (180 mg/l).
Based upon the foregoing waste strength criteria the city would be treating up to nine (9) pounds of BOD and TSS in the base residential rate.
9. In computing any industrial fee, the six thousand (6,000) gallons per month discharge at the normal strength rates set out above shall be used as the
base upon which all industrial user rates shall be based. Any strengths discharged in excess of the normal strength criteria set out above shall be
assessed a surcharge of four cents ($0.04) per twenty five milligrams per liter (25 mg/l) per one thousand (1,000) gallons for all BOD discharged in
excess of the above stated normal strength criteria. A surcharge of two cents ($0.02) per twenty five milligrams per liter (25 mg/l) per one thousand
(1,000) gallons shall be assessed for all of TSS discharged in excess of the above stated normal strength criteria.
10. A surcharge will also be assessed for all discharges in excess of the six thousand (6,000) gallons per month base at the rate of ninety four cents
($0.94) per one thousand (1,000) gallons.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 78/151
11. Any major or minor industry allowed to connect to the city wastewater treatment system shall be monitored by the city no less than annually to
determine whether the estimated monthly flows and strength calculations are equal to or less than those being experienced, and any changes
indicated shall be reflected effective with the month following the date of monitoring.
12. The city reserves the right to refuse to connect any industrial user whose connection would introduce effluent which would:
(a) Be incompatible with;
(b) Contaminate;
(c) Reduce the efficiency of; or
(d) Overload the existing plant.
13. Any special connections not covered by the above schedules shall have fees set by the mayor and council in each individual situation. (Ord. 515, 1-
7-1998)
8-3-19: MEASUREMENT AND SAMPLING OF WATERS AND WASTES:
(A) All significant industrial users shall install a flow measuring device and an automatic sampling device in the building sewer to facilitate observation, flow
measurement and sampling of the wastes. The design and supervision of construction of the "flow measuring and sampling system" shall be by a
professional engineer registered in the state of Idaho. The design, final plans and specifications, and construction of said system must be approved by
the PWD. The industrial user must operate and maintain said system in proper operating condition. The city will read all flow measurements, collect all
samples and perform all testing of collected samples required by the city, Idaho department of health and welfare and the U.S. environmental
protection agency. Users may, at their expense, request additional sampling and testing by the city at a fee established by the PWD.
(B) Any commercial user whose charge is based on water meter readings may install a wastewater flow measuring device or separate water meter as
approved by the PWD at the user's expense, if the water meter readings are not representative of the wastewater flow. The PWD may require a
wastewater system user to install a flow measuring device in the building sewer or water meter if all or part of the water supply to the building comes
from an unmetered source. The user shall operate and maintain such device in proper operating condition.
(C) Sampling and analysis shall be performed in accordance with the techniques prescribed in 40 CFR, part 136, "Standard Methods For Examination Of
Water And Wastewater", and amendments thereto. Where 40 CFR, part 136, "Standard Methods For Examination Of Water And Wastewater" does not
contain sampling or analytical techniques for the pollutant in question, or where EPA determines that the sampling and analytical techniques are
inappropriate for the pollutant in question, sampling and analysis shall be performed by using validated analytical methods or any other applicable
sampling, and analytical procedures, including procedures suggested by the city or other parties, as approved by EPA. Sampling methods, location,
times, durations and frequencies are to generally be determined on an individual basis as shown on the industrial wastewater acceptance form (IWA),
subject to approval by the PWD. For categorical industrial users, sampling frequencies shall be at least as stringent as anyspecified in the applicable
categorical pretreatment standards and industrial waste acceptance agreements. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-20: ADMINISTRATION OF INDUSTRIAL WASTEWATER DISCHARGES:
(A) Wastewater Dischargers: It shall be unlawful to discharge sewage, industrial wastes or other wastes to any sewer within the jurisdiction of the authority,
and/or to the POTW without having first complied with the terms of this chapter.
(B) Disclosure Forms: SIDs (significant industrial dischargers) shall complete and file with the authority, disclosure declaration in the form prescribed by the
authority. Existing SIDs shall file disclosure forms within ninety (90) days after the notice by the city, and proposed new SIDs shall file their disclosure
forms at least ninety (90) days prior to connecting to the POTW. The disclosure to be made by the SID shall be made on written forms provided by the
authority and shall cover:
1. Disclosure of name, address, and location of the discharger.
2. Disclosure of standard industrial classification (SIC) number according to the "Standard Industrial Classification Manual", bureau of the budget,
1972, as amended.
3. Disclosure of wastewater constituents and characteristics including, but not limited to, those mentioned in this chapter, including appendices A and
B, section 8-3-25 of this chapter, as appropriate and as determined by bona fide chemical and biological analyses. Sampling and analysis shall be
performed in accordance with procedures established by the USEPA and contained in standard methods for examination of water and wastewater.
4. Disclosure of time and duration of discharges.
5. Disclosure of average daily and instantaneous peak wastewater flow rates, in gallons per day, including daily, monthly and seasonal variations, if
any. All flows shall be measured, unless other verifiable techniques are approved by authority due to cost or nonfeasibility.
6. Disclosure of site plans, floor plans, mechanical and plumbing plans and details to show all sewers, sewer connections, inspection manholes,
sampling chambers and appurtenances by size, location and elevation.
7. Description of activities, facilities and plant processes on the premises including all materials which are or may be discharged to the sewers or works
of the authority.
8. Disclosure of the nature and concentration of anypollutants or materials prohibited by this chapter in the discharge, together with a statement
regarding whether or not compliance is being achieved with this chapter on a consistent basis and if not, whether additional operation and
maintenance activities and/or additional pretreatment is required for the SID to comply with this chapter.
9. Where additional pretreatment and/or operation and maintenance activities will be required to comply with this chapter, or federal requirements,
whichever are more stringent, the SID shall provide a declaration of the shortest schedule by which the SID will provide such additional pretreatment
and/or implementation of additional operational and maintenance activities.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 79/151
(a) The schedule shall contain milestone dates for the commencement and completion of major events leading to the construction and operation of
additional pretreatment required for SID to comply with the requirements of this chapter including, but not limited to, dates relating to hiring an
engineer, hiring other appropriate personnel, completing preliminary plans, completing final plans, executing contract for major components,
commencing construction, completing construction, and all other acts necessary to achieve compliance with this chapter.
(b) Under no circumstances shall the authority permit a time increment for any single step directed toward compliance which exceeds nine (9)
months.
(c) Not later than fourteen (14) days following each milestone date in the schedule and the final date of compliance, the SID shall submit a progress
report to the authority, including no less than a statement as to whether or not it complied with the increment of progress represented by that
milestone date and, if not, the date on which it expects to comply with this increment of progress, the reason for delay, and the steps being taken
by the SID to return the construction to the approved schedule. In no event shall more than nine (9) months elapse between such progress reports
to the authority.
10. Disclosure of each product produced by type, amount, process or processes and rate of production.
11. Disclosure of the type and amount of raw materials (chemical utilization - average and maximum per day).
12. All disclosure forms shall be signed by a principal executive officer of the SID and a qualified engineer (licensed professional).
13. All sewers shall have an inspection and sampling manhole or structure with an opening of no less than twenty four inches (24") in diameter and an
internal diameter of no less than thirty six inches (36") containing flow measuring, recording and sampling equipment as required by the authorityto
assure compliance with this chapter.
The authority will evaluate the complete disclosure form and data furnished by the SID and may require additional information. Within thirty (30) days
after full evaluation and acceptance of the data furnished, the authority shall notify the SID of the authority's acceptance thereof through issuance of
an industrial wastewater acceptance form.
(C) Industrial Wastewater Acceptance Form (IWA): The PWD shall issue to the SID an IWA which will be based on information in the disclosure form and
include:
1. Any fees and charges to be paid upon initial issuance;
2. Limits on the average and maximum wastewater constituents and characteristics;
3. Limits on average and maximum rate and time of discharge or requirements for flow regulations and equalization;
4. Requirements for installation and maintenance of inspection and sampling facilities;
5. Special conditions as the authority may reasonably require particular circumstances of a given discharge, including sampling locations, frequency of
sampling, number, types, and standards for tests and reporting schedule;
6. Compliance schedules;
7. Requirements for submission of special technical reports or discharge reports where same differs from those prescribed by this chapter;
8. Any special agreements the PWD chooses to continue to develop between the city and SID;
9. Standard conditions as shown in the city's industrial pretreatment study dated January 1984.
All wastewater acceptance forms shall be issued for a period not to exceed five (5) years, subject to amendment or revocation as provided in this
chapter. Under extraordinary circumstances, it may be issued for a stated period or may be stated to expire on a specific date. Wastewater
acceptance forms are issued to a specific SID for a specific operation and are not assignable to another SID or transferable to any other location
without the prior written approval of the authority.
(D) Modifications:
1. Authority's Right: The authority reserves the right toamend this title and the terms and conditions hereof in order to assure compliance by the
authority with applicable laws and regulations. Within nine (9) months of the promulgation of a national categorical pretreatment standard, this title
shall be amended to require compliance by SIDs with such standards within the time frame prescribed by such standards. All national categorical
pretreatment standards adopted after the promulgation of this title shall be adopted by the authority as part of this title. Where a SID subject to a
national categorical pretreatment standard has not previously submitted a disclosure form as required by subsection (C) of this section, the SID shall
file a disclosure form with the authority within one hundred eighty (180) days after the promulgation of the applicable national categorical
pretreatment standard by the USEPA. In addition, any SID operating on the basis of a previous filing of a disclosure statement, shall submit to the
authority within one hundred eighty (180) days after the promulgation of an applicable national categorical pretreatment standard, the additional
information required by subsections (C)8 and (C)9 of this section. The SID shall be informed of any proposed changes in the title at least thirty (30)
days prior to the effective date of change. Any changes or new conditions in the title shall include a reasonable time schedule for compliance.
2. Industrial Wastewater Acceptance: Each SID shall be subject to issuance of a new IWA with appropriate modification if the existing SID changes its
process or its wastewater characteristic.
(E) Reporting Requirements For SID: Within ninety (90) days following the date for final compliance by the SID with applicable standards set forth in this
chapter and following the commencement of the introduction of wastewater into the POTW by a new SID, the SID subject to this chapter shall submit to
the authority a report indicating the nature and concentration of all prohibited or regulated substances contained in its discharge, and the average and
maximum daily flow in gallons. The report shall state whether the applicable pretreatment standards or requirements are being met on a consistent
basis and, if not, what additional operation and maintenance and/or pretreatment is necessary to bring the SID into compliance with the applicable
pretreatment standards or requirements. This statement shall be signed by an authorized representative of the SID.
(F) Periodic Compliance Reports: Any SID subject to a local standard set forth in this chapter, after the compliance date of such pretreatment standard, or,
in the case of a new SID after commencement of the discharge to the authority, shall submit to the authority during the months of June and December,
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 80/151
unless required more frequently by the authority, a report indicating the nature and concentration, of prohibited or regulated substances in the effluent
which are limited by the pretreatment standards hereof. In addition, this report shall include a record of all measured or estimated averageand
maximum daily flows during the reporting period reported in subsection (E) of this section. Flows shall be reported on the basis of actual measurement,
provided however, where cost or feasibility considerations justify, the authority may accept reports of average and maximum flows estimated by
verifiable techniques. The authority, for good cause shown, considering such factors as local high or low flow rates, holidays, budget cycles, or other
extenuating factors may authorize the submission of said reports on months other than those specified above.
Reports of SID's shall contain all results of sampling and analysis of the discharge, including the flow and the nature and concentration or production
and mass where required by the authority. The frequency of monitoring by the SID shall be as prescribed in the industrial waste acceptance form. All
analysis shall be performed in accordance with the standard methods for examination of water and wastewater and amendments thereto.
If standard methods for examination of water and wastewater does not include a sampling or analytical technique for the pollutant in question or where
the EPA determines that the sampling and analytical techniques are inappropriate for the pollutant in question, sampling and analysis shall be
performed by using validated analytical methods or by any other applicable sampling and analytical procedures, including procedures suggested by the
city or other parties, approved by the EPA.
(G) Monitoring Facilities: Each SID shall provide and operate at the SID's own expense, a monitoring facility to allow inspection, sampling, and flow
measurement of each sewer discharge to the authority. Each monitoring facility shall be situated on the SID's premises, except where such a location
would be impractical or cause undue hardship on the SID, the authority may concur with the facility being constructed in the public street or sidewalk
area providing that the facility is located so that it will not be obstructed by landscaping or parked vehicles. There shall be ample room in or near such
sampling facility to allow accurate sampling and preparation of samples for analysis. The facility, sampling, and measuring equipment shall be
maintained at all times in a safe and proper operating condition at the expense of the SID.
All monitoring facilities shall be constructed and maintained in accordance with all applicable local construction standards and specifications.
Construction shall be completed within one hundred twenty (120) days of receipt of an industrial wastewater acceptance form by SID.
(H) Inspection And Sampling: The authority may inspect the monitoring facilities of any SID to determine compliance with the requirements of this chapter.
The SID shall allow the authority or its representatives, upon presentation ofcredentials of identification, to enter upon the premises of the SID at all
reasonable hours, for the purpose of inspection, sampling, or records examination. The authority shall have the right to set up on the SID's property
such devices as are necessary to conduct sampling, inspection, compliance monitoring and/or metering operations.
(I) Confidential Information: Information and data furnished to the authority with respect to the nature and frequency of discharge shall be available to the
public and other governmental agency without restriction unless the SID specifically requests and is able to demonstrate to the satisfaction of the
authority that the release of such information would divulge information, processes or methods of production entitled to protection as trade secrets or
proprietary information of the SID.
When requested by an SID furnishing a report, the portions of a report which may disclose trade secrets or secret processes shall not be made
available for inspection by the public but shall be made available upon written request to governmental agencies for uses related to this chapter, the
national pollutant discharge elimination system (NPDES) permit, the state disposal system permit and/or the pretreatment programs; provided,
however, that such portions of a report shall be available for use by the state or any state agency in judicial review or enforcement proceedings
involving the SID furnishing the report. Wastewater constituents and characteristics will not be recognized as confidential information. Information
accepted by the authority as confidential shall not be transmitted to any governmental agency or to the general public by the authority until and unless
a ten (10) day notification is given to the SID. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-21: FINES AND PENALTIES:
(A) Violation: Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter contained, shall be subject to the provisions of title 1, chapter 3 of this code.
(B) Recovery Of Costs Incurred By The Authority: Any user violating any of the provisions of this chapter who discharges or causes a discharge producing
a deposit or obstruction or causes damage to or impairs the authority's wastewater disposal system shall be liable to the authority for any expense,
loss, or damage caused by such violation or discharge. The authority shall bill the user for the cost incurred by the authority for any cleaning, repair, or
replacement work caused by the violation or discharge. Refusal to pay the assessed costs shall constitute a violation of this chapter, enforceable under
the provisions of this chapter.
(C) Falsifying Information: Any person who knowingly makes anyfalse statement, representation, or certification in any application, record, report, and plan
or other document filed or required to be maintained pursuant to this chapter, or who falsifies, tampers with, or knowingly renders inaccurate any
monitoring device or method required under this chapter, shall (in addition to civil and/or criminal penalties provided by state law) be guilty of a gross
misdemeanor and shall be prosecuted and punished accordingly. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-22: ENFORCEMENT:
(A) Emergency Suspension Of Service And Industrial Wastewater Acceptance Form: The authority may, without advance notice, order the suspension of
the wastewater treatment service to a user, including an SID, and the industrial wastewater acceptance form to an SID when it appears to the authority
that an actual or threatened discharge: 1) presents or threatens an imminent or substantial danger to the health or welfare of persons or substantial
danger to the environment; or 2) threatens to interfere with the operation of the POTW, or to violate any pretreatment limits imposed by this chapter.
Any user notified of the authority's suspension order, shall immediately cease all discharges. In the event of failure of the user to comply with the
suspension order, the authority may commence judicial proceedings immediately thereafter to compel the discharger's specific compliance with such
order and/or to recover civil penalties. The authority shall reinstate the industrial wastewater acceptance form and/or the wastewater treatment service
upon proof by the user of the elimination of the noncomplying discharge or conditions creating the threat as set forth above.
(B) Termination Of Treatment Services: A user shall not:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 81/151
1. Fail to factually report accurately the wastewater constituents and characteristics of its discharge;
2. Fail to report significant changes in wastewater constituents or characteristics;
3. Refuse reasonable access to the discharger's premises by representatives of the authority for the purpose of inspection or monitoring; or
4. Violate the provisions of this chapter, or any order of the authority with respect thereto. The authority may terminate wastewater treatment services to
any user who violates any of the foregoing prohibitions.
(C) Notification Of Violation; Administrative Adjustment: Whenever the authority finds that any user has violated the prohibitions in subsection (B) of this
section, the authority shall cause to be served upon such discharger a written notice (either personally or by certified or registered mail, return receipt
requested) stating the nature of the allegedviolation. Within thirty (30) days of the date of receipt of the notice, the user shall respond personally or in
writing or by certified or registered mail, return receipt requested, to the authority, advising of its position with respect to the allegations. Thereafter, the
user shall be given the opportunity to meet to ascertain the veracity of the allegations and to establish a plan for the satisfactory correction of the
violations and prevention of a recurrence thereof.
(D) Show Cause Hearing: Where the violation of subsection (B) of this section is not corrected by timely compliance by means of administration
adjustment, the authority may order any user which suffers or permits a violation of subsection (B) of this section to show cause before the authority or
its duly authorized representative why the proposed service termination action should not be taken. A written notice shall be served on the user by
personal service, certified or registered mail, return receipt requested, specifying the time and place of a hearing to be held by the authority or its
designee regarding the violation, the reasons why the enforcement action is to be taken, the proposed enforcement action, and directing the user to
show cause before the authority or its designee why the proposed enforcement action should not be taken. The notice of the hearing shall be served
no less than ten (10) days before the hearing. Service may be made on any agent, officer, or authorized representative of a user. The proceedings of
the hearing shall be considered by the authority, which shall then enter appropriate orders with respect to the alleged violations of the user. Appeal of
such orders may be taken by the user in accordance with applicable local or state law.
(E) Judicial Proceedings: Following the entry of any order by the authority with respect to the violation by a user of subsection (B) of this section, the
authority may commence an action for appropriate legal and/or equitable relief in the appropriate local court.
(F) Significant Violations, Annual Publication: A list of users who were significantly violating the terms of this chapter during the previous twelve (12)
months shall be annually published by the city in the largest newspaper published in the city. For the purpose of this section, a "significant violation" is a
violation which remains uncorrected for forty five (45) days after notification of noncompliance; which is part of a pattern of noncompliance over a
twelve (12) month period; which involves a failure to accurately report noncompliance; or which resulted in the city exercising its emergency authority
under subsection (A) of this section.
(G) Right Of Appeal: Any user or any interested party shall have the right to request in writing an interpretation or ruling by the authority on any matter
covered by this chapter and shall be entitled to a prompt written reply. In the event that such inquiry is by a user and deals with matters ofperformance
or compliance with this chapter for which enforcement activity relating to an alleged violation is the subject, receipt of a user's request shall not stay
enforcement proceedings pending. Appeal of any final judicial order entered pursuant to this chapter may be taken in accordance with local and state
law.
(H) Operating Upsets: Any user which experiences an upset in operations which places the user in a temporary state of noncompliance with this chapter
shall inform the authority thereof within twenty four (24) hours of first awareness of the commencement of the upset. Where such information is given
orally, a written follow up report thereof shall be filed by the user with the authority within five (5) days. The report shall specify:
1. Description of the upset, the cause thereof and the upset's impact on the user's compliance status.
2. Duration of noncompliance, including exact dates and times of noncompliance, and if the noncompliance continues, the time by which compliance is
reasonably expected to occur.
3. All steps taken or to be taken to reduce, eliminate and prevent recurrence of such an upset or other conditions of noncompliance. A documented and
verified bona fide operating upset shall be an affirmative defense to any enforcement action brought by the authority against the user for any
noncompliance with this chapter which arises out of violations alleged to have occurred during the period of the upset. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-23: RECORDS RETENTION:
All users subject to this chapter shall retain and preserve for no less than three (3) years any records, books, documents, memoranda, reports,
correspondence, and any and all summaries thereof relating to monitoring, sampling, and chemical analyses made by or in behalf of a user in connection
with its discharge. All records which pertain to matters which are the subject of the administrative adjustment or any other enforcement or litigation
activities brought by the authority pursuant hereto shall be retained and preserved by the user until all enforcement activities have concluded and all
periods of limitations with respect to any and all appeals have expired. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-3-24: PENALTY FOR NONCOMPLIANCE:
If any owner, tenant, occupant or other person connects any possible source of inflow to the sewage collection system that is not permitted by this chapter,
it shall be the responsibility of the city to take the appropriate action to see that the illegal inflow is stopped and the connectionremoved. The city shall also
shut off all water service to the subject property from which the source of inflow originates pending the sealing of the illegal inflow connection. The city may
also bring civil suit against the owner, tenant, occupant, or other person who causes the illegal connection to be made, to recover any and all costs and
damages incurred by the city in terminating the illegal connection.
The owner shall indemnify the city from any loss or damage that may directly or indirectly be occasioned by the installation of a connection except for work
performed by city forces. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
