Chapter 4
MUNICIPAL REFUSE COLLECTION
8-4-1: SHORT TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and may be cited as the MUNICIPAL REFUSE COLLECTION SERVICE CHAPTER OF THE CITY OF AMERICAN FALLS,
IDAHO. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-4-2: DEFINITIONS:
All general definitions1 shall apply to this chapter along with the following definitions which are specific to the refuse collection system:
ASHES: The residue from the burning of wood, coal, coke or other combustible materials.
COLLECTOR: The person holding the contract issued or granted by the city authorizing such person to operate, conduct and maintain a municipal
garbage and refuse collection and disposal system upon, on and over streets, alleys and public ways of the city, or the city of American Falls, Idaho, in the
event the city operates the system.
GARBAGE: Putrescible animal and vegetable waste resulting from the handling, preparation, cooking and consumption of food, grass clippings, paper
packaging products and other items of household waste.
NONCOLLECTIBLE REFUSE: Consists of large, bulky, or heavy items that cannot be handled by the collector's equipment, including, but not limited to:
concrete products, trees and tree limbs, discarded furniture or appliances, engine blocks, dirt, dead animals, rocks, roofing, boards, or any construction or
demolition material, tires, batteries, automobile parts, and waste oil.
OWNER AND OCCUPANT: A person in possession, charge, custody and control of any premises where garbage, refuse and rubbish is collected or
accumulated.
PREMISES: Land and all buildings and structures therein including, but not limited to, by enumeration, single- or multi-family dwellings, rooming houses or
apartment houses, hospitals, convalescent and nursing homes, hotels and motels, restaurants, drive-in establishments, schools and any other place of
habitation, offices, shops or establishments or places of conducting a business, trade or occupation.
REFUSE: All putrescible and nonputrescible solid waste (except body waste), including garbage, rubbish, ashes and street cleanings.
RUBBISH: Nonputrescible solid waste consisting of both combustible and noncombustible waste, such as paper, cardboard, tin cans, yard clippage, wood,
glass, bedding, crockery and similar materials.
SANITARY CONTAINERS: Sanitary containers or receptacles shall be any such containers as shall be approved by the city council and which containers
are compatible with the refuse disposal system and the refuse to be removed. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-4-3: GARBAGE AND REFUSE COLLECTION PROVIDED:
The municipal refuse collection and disposal service of the city shall, by such means as the city council deems appropriate, collect and dispose of all
garbage, rubbish, refuse, paper, glass, tin cans, ashes and other debris; shall operate thereto until duly amended as provided by law. All garbage and
refuse accumulated in the city shall be collected, conveyed and disposed of by the city or its duly authorized contractor. No person shall collect, convey
over any of the streets or alleys of the city or dispose of any refuse accumulated in the city except by the terms of this chapter or resolution of the city
council. However, nothing herein contained shall prohibit any person from hauling their own private refuse from their own property in their own vehicles at
their expense without penalty; provided, that said removal by said person shall not reduce or otherwise affect that person's obligation to pay the sanitary
service fees hereinafter set out; provided, also, that all such hauling shall be in vehicles that meet the requirements of section8-4-10 of this chapter. The
right and power to amend this chapter from time to time and to repeal the same is reserved to the city. The city may from time to time grant an exclusive
contract for the operation of the municipal refuse collection and disposal service. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-4-4: MANDATORY COLLECTION:
(A) Collection From Entire City: All garbage, refuse, rubbish and ashes from the entire residential, commercial and industrial sections of the city property
placed for collection as provided for herein, shall be collected by the city or its duly authorized contractor necessary to maintain and preserve sanitation
of the community. Temporary failure to make such collection due to circumstances beyond the control of the city shall not relieve the occupant or the
owner of the premises from the payment of sanitary service fees herein prescribed.
(B) Collection And Disposal Service Compulsory; Exemption: No person shall be permitted to refuse to accept the refuse collection and disposal service
herein provided for, and the failure of any person to receive or use such service shall not exempt such person from the payment of charges herein
specified, except as provided in subsection 8-4-8(C) of this chapter. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-4-5: PUBLIC WORKS DIRECTOR TO PUBLISH RULES AND REGULATIONS:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 87/151
The PWD is hereby empowered to prepare and publish such rules and regulations as may be necessary in connection with the municipal refuse collection
and garbage collection and disposal service subject to the approval of the city council and may direct that the city garbage and waste disposal crew or
authorized contractor will not collect garbage and other wastes from premises where rules and regulations are not complied with, and the failure to collect
the same by direction shall not relieve the owner or occupant from the payment of fees or penalties provided for in this chapter. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-4-6: CONTAINERS:
(A) Requirements: Sanitary containers or containers authorized under this section shall be provided by the city. All containers shall be maintained by the
user in good condition and at ground level. The city inspector shall have authority to refuse collection service for failure to comply herewith. It shall be
the duty of the user to maintain the same in a reasonably sanitary condition in keeping with reasonable health standards. The city inspector shall have
the responsibility of inspecting containers and to notify the user for failure to maintain the same in a reasonably sanitary condition. It is the responsibility
of the user to pay for anyand all container damages caused by their negligence, abuse or neglect.
(B) Garbage Placement: All garbage shall be placed in "sanitary containers" as defined in section 8-4-2 of this chapter. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-4-7: PLACEMENT OF CONTAINERS:
The garbage, refuse and rubbish in and about any private residence, dwelling house, commercial or industrial building shall be placed in sanitary
containers and shall be placed at ground level near the alley line if there is a public alley right of way, unless the city inspector determines otherwise, or if
there is no access to the alley from the dwelling or other buildings, then such sanitary containers shall be placed at street level so as to be easily seen and
at the curb line. Refuse generating property not abutting public streets or alleys shall permit ground level access to the city or its refuse placed thereon in
approved sanitary containers. Placement of containers in unusual circumstances will be determined by the city inspector. The sanitary containers placed
on streets where there is no alley access shall be removed from the street within twenty four (24) hours after pick up. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-4-8: SANITARY SERVICE FEES:
Fees for sanitary service shall be set from time to time by resolution of the city council.
(A) All commercial customers shall use such containers either alone or sharing with other customers as prescribed by the city council.
(B) Residential customers shall use such containers as shall be approved by the city council and as directed by the city inspector. In directing the size to
use, the city inspector shall consider alley or front pick up accessibility to customer use, density of surrounding population, availability of joint use with
others.
(C) The city council may grant variances from the provisions hereto, if necessary, for users having noncollectible refuse who, in the opinion of the city
council, are unable to comply with provisions of this chapter. In that event the council must state why compliance is impossible, and the acts required of
the user for the noncollectible refuse removal, the charges, if any therefor, and the duration of the grant of variance. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-4-9: USE OF STREETS AND ALLEYS:
No person shall be permitted to transport garbage, refuse, rubbish or ashes over the streets and alleys of the city in anything other than secured or
covered vehicles. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-4-10: STORING REFUSE, CLEANUP DAYS:
(A) No person shall place any garbage, rubbish or refuse in any street, alley or other public place or upon any private property, whether owned by such
person or not, within the city, except that placed in proper containers at ground level for collection, under the method provided pursuant to the authority
of this chapter. Any unauthorized accumulation of refuse, garbage or rubbish on any premises is hereby declared to be a nuisance and is prohibited.
Failure to remove any existing accumulation of refuse within twenty four (24) hours after notice from the city shall be deemed a violation of this chapter.
(B) No person shall cast, place, sweep or deposit anywhere within the city any refuse or garbage in such a manner that it may be carried or deposited by
the elements upon any street, sidewalk, alley or other public place or in or on any occupied premises within the city. The city may authorize storage of
refuse on streets and alleys for spring and fall cleanup. The city shall designate such places and times where such accumulation is allowed by
resolution. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-4-11: STREET LITTER CONTAINERS:
Public street litter and waste disposal containers are not to be used by merchants and store employees for store and sidewalk sweepings, trash, papers or
cartons. They are placed there by the city for pedestrians to use in the depositing of waste material to prevent the same from littering upon the city
sidewalks and street gutters. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-4-12: UNAUTHORIZED USE OF CONTAINERS:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 88/151
It shall be unlawful for anyone not authorized by the city to deposit waste material in any city owned garbage containers. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-4-13: CONSTRUCTION DEBRIS:
Debris resulting from the construction, reconstruction or repair of premises shall not be placed with other refuse for collection but shall be disposed of
directly by the person owning, occupying or leasing the premises. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-4-14: UNACCEPTABLE TRASH:
Unacceptable trash shall include demolition materials, concrete block, dirt, rocks, roofing boards, tires, batteries, automobile parts, waste oil, any
hazardous waste materials, tree limbs, tree trunks, Christmas trees, hot ashes, dead animals or animal parts, commercial or industrial wastes such as
waste grain, potato waste, slaughterhouse waste, and any other such trash as designated by the PWD. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-4-15: INTERFERE WITH CITY INSPECTOR:
It shall be unlawful for any person to interfere with or obstruct the city inspector during the performance of his duties under this chapter. (Ord. 515, 1-7-
1998)
8-4-16: SUPPRESSING NUISANCES:
The city inspector shall take cognizance of all nuisances within the limits of the city and shall take such measures as may be effectual to suppress and
abate the same. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
8-4-17: APPEALS:
Any person aggrieved by regulations under this chapter, by the city inspector, or any contractor whom the city has contracted for the garbage and refuse
collection may appeal to the city council. Such appeal shall be perfected by filing a written specification of grievances with the city clerk-treasurer. Within a
period of not less than ten (10) nor more than thirty (30) days, the city council shall meet to hear such appeal. Notice of the time and place of hearing shall
be given to the person appealing at the address shown on the person's notice of appeal. The city council shall hear all parties in interest and shall issue its
order, its findings of fact and conclusions and order based thereon. Decision of the city council shall be final. (Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
Title 9
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
Chapter 1
SIDEWALKS AND CURBS
9-1-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purposes of this chapter, these words are defined as follows:
CURB: A raised edging along a sidewalk which separates the street surface from the sidewalk, usually constructed of concrete. The curb may include a
gutter, in which case the curb and gutter casting is considered a curb for purposes of this chapter.
SIDEWALK: That area of public right of way between the back of the curb line and private property line, along any public street or alley, with or without an
existing concrete structure thereon. The sidewalk includes any driveway approach. (Ord. 530, 12-7-1998)
9-1-2: SPECIFICATIONS:
The specifications in the Idaho standards for public works construction, as amended, shall govern all construction and/or repair of curbs and sidewalks
within the municipality. (Ord. 530, 12-7-1998)
9-1-3: OWNER'S DUTY TO CONSTRUCT, REPAIR OR REPLACE:
It is the duty of the person owning or having control of real property along or abutting any curb or sidewalk, to construct, repair or replace the curb or
sidewalk so as to provide safe, all-weather passage for pedestrians, and to provide adequate street drainage and pavement protection, for the safety and
convenience of the traveling public. (Ord. 530, 12-7-1998)
9-1-4: CITY'S ABILITY TO REQUIRE CONSTRUCTION, REPAIR OR REPLACEMENT:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 89/151
If the city council finds that curbs or sidewalks are dangerous and unsafe, requiring construction, repair or replacement thereof, the council may, at its
option:
(A) Serve written notice on the owner or person in control of the real property adjacent to the curb or sidewalk, informing that person of the unsafe
condition and requiring that person to construct, repair, or replace the curb or sidewalk as specified by the council, or, provide a plan acceptable to the
building administrator, within twenty one (21) days after receipt of the notice. In the event the necessary construction, repair, or replacement does not
take place, the council may proceed according to subsection (B) of this section; or
(B) Provide, by general ordinance, for the construction, repair, or replacement of the unsafe curb or sidewalk, and assess the cost thereof to the adjacent
property. Collection of the assessment may be done pursuant to Idaho Code section 50-1008. Nothing herein shall preclude the council from
establishing a local improvement district for the construction, repair or replacement of curbs and sidewalks, pursuant to chapter 17, title 50 of the Idaho
Code. (Ord. 530, 12-7-1998)
Chapter 2
REMOVAL OF SNOW AND/OR ICE
9-2-1: REMOVAL OF SNOW AND/OR ICE:
It shall be the duty of the owner or tenant of any premises abutting or adjoining any public sidewalk to remove all snow and/or ice from such sidewalk.
(1960 Code)
9-2-2: NOTICE TO BE GIVEN:
It shall be the duty of the municipality to give notice to any owner or tenant of any property to remove snow and/or ice, which notice shall be sent by
registered mail to the last known address of such owner, tenant or occupant. The owner or occupant shall have not more than twenty four (24) hours from
and after receipt of such notice, within which to remove the snow and/or ice as set forth in said notice. (1960 Code)
9-2-3: UPON FAILURE TO COMPLY, MUNICIPALITY TO REMOVE:
Upon failure of an owner or tenant to comply with the provisions of this chapter, the municipality shall have the right to remove such snow and/or ice and
assess the cost thereof against the premises abutting the sidewalk. Such assessment to be certified to the county assessor or other proper county official
having charge of the making of the assessment roll, and such charge shall be placed on the assessment roll and collected in the same manner as other
municipal taxes are collected. (1960 Code)
Chapter 3
TREES AND SHRUBBERY
9-3-1: TREES TO BE TRIMMED:
Any owner or occupant of any real property shall trim all trees on property owned or occupied by him, overhanging any public thoroughfare, so that the
branches thereon will not interfere with pedestrians or public travel. (1960 Code)
9-3-2: HEDGES AND SHRUBBERY:
Any owner or occupant of any real property shall maintain all hedges and shrubbery adjacent to public sidewalks so that no part of said hedges and/or
shrubbery shall extend over any part of a public sidewalk in the municipality. (1960 Code)
9-3-3: INJURY TO TREES AND/OR SHRUBBERY:
It is hereby declared unlawful for any person, not the owner thereof, or without lawful authority so to do, wilfully to injure, deface, disfigure or destroy any
tree or shrub, or to injure, destroy, cut or pick any flower or plant, located either on private ground or on any public place or thoroughfare. (1960 Code)
9-3-4: TREES OUTSIDE OF PROPERTY LINE:
The governing body of the municipality is hereby provided full and complete control over all trees which are outside the property lines of privately owned
real property. (1960 Code)
Chapter 4
WEED AND WASTE MATTER ABATEMENT
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 90/151
9-4-1: TITLE, CITATION:
This chapter shall be known and shall be cited as the CITY OF AMERICAN FALLS WEED AND WASTE MATTER ABATEMENT ORDINANCE. (Ord. 443,
7-11-1990)
9-4-2: NUISANCE, PROHIBITED:
No owner of any lot, place or area within the city, or occupant or person in control of same, shall permit on such lot, place or area or upon any street,
sidewalk or public right of way abutting the same, a public nuisance to exist as herein defined and found to exist by the fire chief or his authorized
representative, or the chief of police or his authorized representative. (Ord. 443, 7-11-1990)
9-4-3: PUBLIC NUISANCES DESIGNATED:
(A) All weeds, dry grasses, trees, shrubs and other vegetation, rubbish, refuse, garbage, trash or any material present upon the streets, sidewalks,
adjacent public rights of way or upon private property within the city, which by reason of size, manner of growth, or location, constitutes a fire hazard to
any building, improvements, crops or other property, as well as weeds and other vegetation, which by reason of promiscuous propagation are likely to
cause damage to public streets and sidewalks, or which interferes with the reasonable enjoyment of property by the neighbors, are declared to be a
public nuisance.
(B) Regularly cultivated, mowed and useful grasses and pastures shall not be declared a public nuisance. However, if the fire chief or his authorized
representative determines it necessary to protect adjacent improved property from fire exposure, an adequate fire break may be required.
(C) "Waste matter" as hereinafter defined, which by reason of its location and character is unsightly or which interferes with the reasonable enjoyment of
property by the neighbors, or which would materially hamper or interfere with the prevention or suppression of fire upon the premises, or any adjoining
premises, or the abatement of a nuisance as defined by this chapter is declared a public nuisance.
(D) "Waste matter" is defined for the purpose of this chapter as unused or discarded matter having little or no substantial market value, which is exposed to
the elements and/or is not enclosed in any structure or otherwise completely concealed from public view, and which consists (without limitation or
exclusion by enumeration) of such matter and material as:
1. Rubble: To include asphalt, concrete, plaster, tile, dirt, and/or gravel piles, unused building or mobile home foundations;
2. Rubbish: To include crates, cartons, metal and glass containers, newspapers, boxes, wood shavings, lumber scraps, bedding, lawn clippings,
furniture, home appliances, washers, dryers, freezers, refrigerators, dilapidated outbuildings, fragments of buildings; and
3. Vehicular Components: To include automotive bodies, trailers, tires, farm equipment, and commercial equipment components and/or parts thereof.
(Ord. 443, 7-11-1990)
9-4-4: NUISANCE ABATEMENT NOTICE:
If it is determined by the fire chief or his authorized representative, or the chief of police or his authorized representative that a "public nuisance", as herein
defined, exists on any lot, place or area, or upon any street, sidewalk, or public right of way abutting the same, the chief of the fire department or the chief
of police or an authorized representative shall cause a notice to be issued to abate such nuisance. Such notice shall be headed "Notice To Clean
Premises"; shall contain a description of the property in general terms reasonably sufficient to identify the location of the nuisance; shall describe the
nuisance in terms reasonably sufficient to identify the same; shall direct the abatement of the nuisance; shall specify the penalty provision as provided
herein; and shall specify the appeal process as provided herein. Such notice may be on a form prescribed by the city. (Ord. 443, 7-11-1990)
9-4-5: ABATEMENT NOTICE, SERVICE:
The notice required by section 9-4-4 of this chapter may be served in the following manner:
(A) By personal service on the owner of said lot, place, or area, if the owner lives within the city, and by personal service on the occupant or person in
charge or control of the property, if such person can be identified; or
(B) If said owner does not live within the city, by registered mail to the owner at the address shown on the last available assessment roll, or as otherwise
known; and, by personal service on the occupant or person in charge or control of the property, if such person can be identified; or
(C) Should the owner not be known or have an available address, by posting at a conspicuous place on the land or abutting a public right of way and by
publication of said notice at least once a week for the period of two (2) weeks in a newspaper of general circulation in the city and by personal service
on the occupant or person in charge or control of the property, if such person can be identified. Said newspaper advertisement shall be a general notice
that property in the city has been posted in accordance with this chapter and contain a general statement of the effect of such postings. The date of
such newspaper advertisements shall not be considered in computing the appeal periods provided by this chapter. (Ord. 443, 7-11-1990)
9-4-6: APPEAL:
Within ten (10) days from the date of posting, mailing, or personal service of the required notice, the owner or person occupying or controlling such lot,
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 91/151
place or area affected may appeal to the city council. Such appeal shall be in writing and shall be filed with the city clerk. At the regular meeting, or
recessed meeting of the city council, not less than ten (10) days nor more than twenty six (26) days thereafter, the city council shall proceed to hear and
pass upon such appeal, and the decision of the city council thereupon shall be final and conclusive. (Ord. 443, 7-11-1990)
9-4-7: ABATEMENT REQUIRED, TIME LIMIT:
It shall be the duty of the owner or person occupying or controlling any lot, place or area in the city which has been declared a public nuisance as provided
herein, within ten (10) days from the date of notification as provided herein, or in case of an appeal to the city council, within ten (10) days from the
determination thereof, unless the same is sustained, to remove the nuisance as stated. (Ord. 443, 7-11-1990)
9-4-8: VIOLATION, PENALTIES:
(A) Failure to abate the stated nuisance shall be a misdemeanor.
(B) Any chronic nuisance shall be a misdemeanor. A chronic nuisance occurs any time a property receives two (2) or more nuisance abatement notices for
a substantially similar or related nuisance activity within a three hundred sixty five (365) day period.
(C) The provisions of this chapter are not exclusive remedies and the city may invoke all remedies, civil and criminal, provided for abatement of nuisances.
(Ord. 597, 2-3-2010)
9-4-9: ABATEMENT BY CITY, COSTS:
Upon the failure to abate a stated nuisance within the time limits of section 9-4-7 of this chapter, the city may remove the same, doing whatever is
necessary to accomplish the abatement cleanup, removal and related work. The costs thereof may be assessed against the property and collected as
provided by law, particularly as provided by Idaho Code title 50, chapter 10, "Special Assessments", or the city may collect the costs by civil action. (Ord.
443, 7-11-1990)
9-4-10: SEVERABILITY:
If any section, paragraph, clause, or provision of this chapter is held to be invalid for any reason, such invalidation shall not affect the validity and
enforceability of any of the remaining provisions hereof. (Ord. 443, 7-11-1990)
Chapter 5
STREETS AND ALLEYS CONTINUOUS
9-5-1: STREETS AND ALLEYS CONTINUOUS:
Streets and alleys laid out in any addition to the city shall be continuous with and correspond in directions and width to the streets and alleys of the city to
which they are an addition. (1960 Code)
Chapter 6
SIGNS AND AWNINGS
9-6-1: MANNER OF CONSTRUCTION:
(A) Signs erected over the sidewalk shall be constructed entirely of metal not lighter than N. 28 U.S. gauge, or other equally substantial material. Frames
shall be constructed of angles or other rolled steel shapes not thinner than N. 20 U.S. gauge steel. The lower edge of any such sign shall not be less
than eight feet (8') from the sidewalk and such sign shall not extend horizontally to within one foot (1') of sidewalk width.
(B) All signs shall be supported from the buildings in front of which they are placed with proper metal supports securely bolted or fastened to masonry
walls. All signs extending over the sidewalk shall be laterally secured with guywires which are made adjustable by means of turnbuckles. Where
buildings set back of the property line, signs may be mounted on a single steel pole that is securely anchored in concrete.
(C) The framework of all boards or signs placed upon the roof of any building or structure shall be of iron or steel and shall be so constructed and fastened
to the roof as to be capable of withstanding a wind pressure of not less than twenty (20) pounds per square foot of surface area. Said board or sign
shall be set back from the firewall of said building or structure a distance of least three feet (3') so as to leave a clear passageway around and in front
of the same. The bottom line of the surface of said board or sign shall be at least four feet (4') in the clear above the roof of said building so as to leave
a clear passageway under the same. (1960 Code)
9-6-2: AWNINGS, ERECTION OF:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 92/151
It shall be unlawful for any person or persons, firm or corporation to erect, construct or maintain within the city any awning or covering over any sidewalk
except folding awnings and those that are raised by means of rollers, constructed of cloth or canvas, placed upon substantial iron or wood frames and
securely fastened to the building. The lower edge of the frame of any such awning shall be not less than seven feet (7') from the sidewalk, and the lower
edge of the cloth or canvas skirt of such awning shall be not less than six and one-half feet (61/2') from the sidewalk. (1960 Code)
9-6-3: BANNERS ON AWNINGS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to place any banner of any kind whatsoever upon any awning over any sidewalk in the city, the lower edge of which
banner extends below the lower edge of the awning on which it is hung. (1960 Code)
Chapter 7
REFUSE IN BUILDINGS; STAGNANT WATER
9-7-1: REFUSE IN BUILDINGS; STAGNANT WATER:
No person shall permit or suffer to be in or accumulate in, or upon any yard, lot, place or premises or upon any street or sidewalk adjacent to or abutting
upon any lot, block, place or premises, or in any building or shed owned or occupied by him or them or for which he or they may be agents within the limits
of the city, any stagnant water or impure water, refuse, vegetable decay or decaying substance, garbage or filth of any kind, nor suffer such yard, lot,
place, building or premises to be or to remain in such condition as to cause or create a nuisance or offensive smell or to pollute or render unhealthful the
atmosphere or the premises or hereby to be, become, cause or create a public nuisance. (1960 Code; amd. Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
Chapter 8
UNSAFE BUILDINGS
9-8-1: ADOPTION OF RESOLUTION:
In order for the city council to avail itself of the remedies provided in Idaho Code sections 50-334, 50-335 and 50-1008, it shall first adopt a resolution
declaring that it deems a nuisance to exist, as provided in Idaho Code section 50-334, or that a building or structure is, in the opinion of the city council, so
dilapidated or is in such condition as to menace the public health or the safety of persons or property on account of increased fire hazard or otherwise, as
provided in Idaho Code section 50-335. (Ord. 320, 12-1974; amd. Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
9-8-2: PUBLIC HEARING:
Thereafter, the city council shall hold a public hearing at which any person interested in the alleged nuisance or in the property may appear and object to
the designation of nuisance or menace to public health or the safety of persons or property. (Ord. 320, 12-1974; amd. Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
9-8-3: NOTICE OF HEARING:
Notice of the aforesaid hearing shall be given by certified mail to all persons, associations, corporations or copartnerships holding, owning or maintaining
the property, building or structure declared to be a nuisance or a menace to public health or property. No such hearing shall be held and no further action
taken until twenty (20) days after such notice shall have been regularly deposited in the United States mail. (Ord. 320, 12-1974; amd. Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
9-8-4: FINAL DETERMINATION:
After such hearing the city council shall make a final determination as to whether a nuisance exists or that the building or structure menaces the public
health or safety. (Ord. 320, 12-1974; amd. Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
9-8-5: NOTICE, TIME LIMIT FOR REMOVAL:
If the city council determines that a nuisance exists or that a building or structure menaces the public health or safety, notice thereof shall be given in the
manner and to the persons specified in section 9-8-3 of this chapter. Said persons shall be advised that they will have a reasonable time, to be specified
by the city council, within which to abate the nuisance or repair or remove the building or structure or suffer the same to be done by the city and the cost
thereof assessed against the property upon which the nuisance, building or structure is situated as provided in Idaho Code section 50-1008. (Ord. 320, 12-
1974; amd. Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)
Chapter 9
WATER RATES
(Rep. by Ord. 515, 1-7-1998)

Chapter 10
EXCAVATING
9-10-1: LICENSE TO EXCAVATE:
No person shall dig or excavate in any street or alley in the city of American Falls without first obtaining a license therefor from the city clerk. (Ord. 319, 7-
17-1974)
9-10-2: BOND REQUIRED:
As a prerequisite to the issuing of such license, the city clerk shall require a fee in an amount to be set by the city council together with a refundable fee,
bond or undertaking from the applicant in such form as required by the city council, which said refundable fee, bond or undertaking shall be to guarantee
that the street or alley be returned to its former condition within a reasonable time after the digging or excavation permitted by the license. (Ord. 581, 8-16-
2006)
9-10-3: VIOLATION:
Violation of this chapter shall be deemed a misdemeanor. (Ord. 319, 7-17-1974)
Chapter 11
TREE PLANTING, PROTECTION AND REMOVAL
9-11-1: PURPOSE:
It is the purpose of this chapter to promote and protect the public health, safety, and general welfare by providing for the regulation of the planting,
maintenance, and removal of trees, shrubs, and other plants within the city of American Falls. (Ord. 598, 2-3-2010)
9-11-2: DEFINITIONS:
HAZARDOUS TREES OR SHRUBS: Those with dead limbs or branches which could fall and cause hazard to anyone on public property.
PEST INFESTED TREES OR SHRUBS: Any tree or shrub that, because of disease from pests, can affect the health of other trees and shrubs within the
city.
PUBLIC TREE OR SHRUB: Any tree or shrub on any public property or right of way.
THREAT: A "threat" consists of any destructive or communicable disease or other pestilence which endangers the growth or health of trees and/or shrubs.
TREE TOPPING: The improper pruning or severe cutting back of limbs within a tree's crown or the removal of the top portion of the trunk of a tree. (Ord.
598, 2-3-2010)
9-11-3: TREE BOARD:
(A) Authority And Power:
1. A city tree board for the city of American Falls, state of Idaho, shall be created and established, consisting of five (5) members, citizens and residents
who reside or work within Power County, who shall be appointed by the mayor with the approval of the city council. Members of the board shall serve
without compensation in an advisory capacity to the city council.
2. It shall be the responsibility of the board to study, investigate, counsel and develop planting, replanting, removal or disposition of trees and shrubs in
parks, along streets and in other public areas. Such plan will be presented to the city council for their acceptance and approval. The plan shall also
be delivered to the city building administrator for consideration and guidance on issuance of building permits, subdivision permits, and other planning
and building matters.
(B) Term Of Office:
1. The term of the five (5) board members to be appointed by the mayor are:
(a) One member will serve for one year;
(b) Two (2) members will serve for two (2) years;
(c) Two (2) members will serve for three (3) years.
2. If any board member leaves the board before his/her term is finished, a successor shall be appointed by the mayor for the remainder of that term.
After the expiration of the initial terms of office, members shall be appointed for three (3) year terms of office. (Ord. 598, 2-3-2010)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 94/151
9-11-4: APPLICABILITY:
The plan shall include all trees, plants and shrubs located within street rights of way, parks, golf courses, buffer zones, and public lands within the city
limits, and to trees, plants and shrubs located on private property that constitute a hazard or threat as described in this chapter. (Ord. 598, 2-3-2010)
9-11-5: LICENSING AND INSURANCE:
City trees and shrubs shall be maintained by qualified city employees or under the direction of a certified arborist that is licensed and insured. (Ord. 598, 2-
3-2010)
9-11-6: LANDSCAPING:
All new development shall include parkway trees from the small and medium tree list of recommended trees and shrubs developed by the board. Tree
plantings shall comply with the "site vision triangle" of intersections and at proper setback distances. (Ord. 598, 2-3-2010)
9-11-7: TREE PLANTING, MAINTENANCE AND REMOVAL:
The planting, maintenance, and removal of all public trees in parks and recreational areas of the city shall be done within the guidelines and standards set
forth by the board. (Ord. 598, 2-3-2010)
9-11-8: TREE PROTECTION:
The following guidelines and standards shall apply to trees on public property, in the tree protection plan:
(A) It shall be prohibited for any person, firm, or city department to "top" any public trees.
(B) All planting and removal of public trees or shrubs should be done according to the work plan prepared for the city by the board.
(C) No disposal of toxic waste matter shall be placed within the proximity of the root zone of any trees or shrubs.
(D) No attached devices or structures (i.e., tree houses or signs) may be placed on trees.
(E) Trees and shrubs will be pruned or removed in accordance with the definition of "clear vision triangle" contained in the American Falls development
code, section 11-16-2 of this code. (Ord. 598, 2-3-2010)
9-11-9: ENFORCEMENT AND PENALTIES:
Upon the discovery of a "threat" as defined herein, the city building administrator shall at once cause written notice to be served upon the owner of the
property upon which such diseased or infested tree is situated, by personal service, or certified mail, return receipt requested, and the notice shall state
that such condition must be cured by the property owner within ten (10) days from the date of the official notice or the threat may be treated as a nuisance
and may be abated by the city with all costs of abatement assessed against the property owner. The property owner may appeal the building
administrator's decision to the city council by lodging written notice with the city clerk within such ten (10) day period. The hearing shall be held within
seven (7) days after the city clerk receives the property owner's written request. The hearing shall be informal and strict rules of evidence shall not apply.
The property owner may be represented by counsel; present oral and written evidence and cross examine witnesses. The city council shall issue a
decision within three (3) days after the close of the hearing and shall notify the property owner in writing of the decision. If the city council upholds the city
building administrator's determination that a threat exists, the threat shall be abated by the city and all costs of abatement shall be assessed against the
property owner. The decision of the city council is final.
The city shall also have the authority to enforce any provisions of this chapter by civil and/or criminal proceedings.
Where it has been determined that a public tree(s) has been damaged or removed in violation of this chapter and/or Idaho Code 6-202, the offending
person or firm shall be assessed treble the cost of repair or replacement. The city shall determine that cost using accepted plant appraisal methods as set
forth in the current edition of the "Guide For Plant Appraisal", published by the International Society Of Arboriculture.
Any person, partnership, firm, corporation or other legal entity that violates any provision of this chapter is guilty of a misdemeanor and may also be fined a
sum not to exceed one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) for any one offense and may be confined in the municipal jail for a period of not more than six (6)
months. All violations, which are of a continuing nature, shall constitute a separate offense for each day of such continuance. (Ord. 598, 2-3-2010)
Title 10
TRAFFIC
Chapter 1
ADOPTION OF IDAHO MOTOR VEHICLE LAWS
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 95/151
10-1-1: INTENT:
It is hereby declared to be the intent of the governing body of the city to aid and assist by whatever means possible, for the utmost consistency in traffic
regulation among and between agencies of Idaho having such jurisdiction. Toward that end, adoption of the Idaho motor vehicle laws by the cities of Idaho
is a necessary means of assuring maximum uniformity within the state. (Ord. 287, 12-16-1970, eff. 1-2-1971)
10-1-2: ADOPTION OF IDAHO MOTOR VEHICLE LAWS:
There is hereby adopted for the purpose of establishing rules and regulations for the use of all streets and public thoroughfares of the city that certain
code, identified as the 1969 revised edition, Idaho motor vehicle laws, more particularly title 49, Idaho Code, published by the department of law
enforcement, and as the same may hereafter be revised by the Idaho legislature, or amended by the governing body, and the same is hereby adopted and
incorporated as an ordinance of the city as fully as though set forth at length herein. (Ord. 287, 12-16-1970, eff. 1-2-1971)
10-1-3: COPIES TO BE KEPT ON FILE:
Three (3) copies of the Idaho motor vehicle laws, together with any revisions or amendments, duly certified by the city clerk, shall be kept on file in his
office for use and examination of and by the public. (Ord. 287, 12-16-1970, eff. 1-2-1971)
Chapter 2
BICYCLES
10-2-1: EFFECT OF REGULATIONS:
(A) It shall be unlawful for any person to do any act forbidden or fail to perform any act required herein.
(B) The parent of any child and the guardian of any ward shall not authorize or knowingly permit any such child or ward to violate any of the provisions of
this chapter.
(C) These regulations applicable to bicycles shall apply whenever a bicycle is operated upon any public thoroughfare or public path set aside for the
exclusive use of bicycles. (1960 Code)
10-2-2: LICENSE REQUIRED:
It shall be unlawful for any person residing in the municipality, to ride or propel a bicycle on any public thoroughfare unless such bicycle has been licensed
and a license plate is attached thereto. (1960 Code)
10-2-3: LICENSE APPLICATION:
Application for a bicycle license and license plate shall be made to the clerk. A fee of one dollar ($1.00) per annum shall be paid before such license is
issued. (1960 Code)
10-2-4: ISSUANCE OF LICENSE:
(A) The clerk, upon receiving proper application therefor, is authorized to issue a bicycle license which shall be effective until the end of the calendar year.
(B) The clerk shall not issue a license for any bicycle when he knows the applicant is not the owner of or entitled to the possession of such bicycle.
(C) The clerk shall keep a record of the number of each license, the date issued, the name and address of the person to whom issued, the number on the
frame of the bicycle and a record of all bicycle license fees collected. (1960 Code)
10-2-5: ATTACHMENT OF LICENSE PLATE:
(A) The clerk, upon issuing a bicycle license, shall also issue a license plate bearing the license number assigned to the bicycle, the name of the
municipality and the calendar year for which issued.
(B) Each license plate shall be firmly attached to the bicycle in such a position as to be plainly visible.
(C) It shall be unlawful for any person to remove a license plate from a bicycle during the period for which issued except upon a transfer of ownership or in
the event the bicycle is dismantled. (1960 Code)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 96/151
10-2-6: INSPECTION:
The clerk shall inspect each bicycle before licensing the same and shall refuse a license for any bicycle which he determines is in unsafe mechanical
condition. (1960 Code)
10-2-7: RENEWAL OF LICENSE:
Upon the expiration of any bicycle license the same may be renewed upon application and payment of the same fee as upon the original application.
(1960 Code)
10-2-8: TRANSFER OF OWNERSHIP:
Upon the sale or transfer of a licensed bicycle the licensee shall remove the plate and shall either surrender the same to the clerk or may upon proper
application, but without payment of an additional fee, have said plate assigned to another bicycle owned by the applicant. (1960 Code)
10-2-9: RENTAL AGENCIES:
A rental agency shall not rent or offer any bicycle for rent unless the bicycle is licensed and a license plate is attached thereto. (1960 Code)
10-2-10: BICYCLE DEALERS:
Every person engaged in the business of buying or selling new or secondhand bicycles shall make a report to the clerk of every bicycle purchased or sold
by such dealer, giving the name and address of the person from whom purchased or to whom sold, a description of such bicycle by name or make, the
frame number thereof, and the number of license plate, if any, found thereon. (1960 Code)
10-2-11: TRAFFIC LAWS APPLY:
Every person riding a bicycle upon a roadway shall be granted all of the rights and shall be subject to all of the duties applicable to the driver of a vehicle,
except as to special regulations in this chapter and except as to those provisions of this title which by their nature can have no application. (1960 Code)
10-2-12: OBEDIENCE TO TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES:
(A) Any person operating a bicycle shall obey the instructions of official traffic control signs, signals and other control devices applicable to vehicles unless
otherwise directed by a police officer.
(B) Whenever authorized signs are erected indicating that no right, left or U-turn is permitted, it shall be unlawful for any person operating a bicycle to
disobey the direction of any such sign; except, where a person dismounts from the bicycle to make such turn, in which event such person shall then
obey the regulations applicable to pedestrians. (1960 Code)
10-2-13: RIDING ON BICYCLES:
(A) A person propelling a bicycle shall not ride other than upon or astride a permanent and regular seat attached thereto.
(B) No bicycle shall be used to carry more persons at one time than the number for which it is designed and equipped. (1960 Code)
10-2-14: RIDING ON ROADWAYS AND BICYCLE PATHS:
(A) Every person operating a bicycle upon a roadway shall ride asnear to the right side of the roadway as practicable, exercising due care when passing a
standing vehicle or one proceeding in the same direction.
(B) Persons riding bicycles upon a roadway shall not ride more than two (2) abreast except on paths or parts of roadways set aside for the exclusive use of
bicycles.
(C) Whenever a usable path for bicycles has been provided adjacent to a roadway, bicycle riders shall use such path and shall not use the roadway. (1960
Code)
10-2-15: SPEED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a bicycle at a speed greater than is reasonable and prudent under the conditions then existing. (1960 Code)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 97/151
10-2-16: EMERGING FROM ALLEY OR DRIVEWAY:
The operator of a bicycle emerging from an alley, driveway or building shall, upon approaching a sidewalk or the sidewalk area extending across any
alleyway, yield the right of way to all pedestrians approaching on said sidewalk and upon entering the roadway shall yield the right of way to all vehicles
approaching on said roadway. (1960 Code)
10-2-17: CLINGING TO VEHICLES:
It shall be unlawful for any person riding upon any bicycle to attach the same or himself to any vehicle upon any public thoroughfare. (1960 Code)
10-2-18: CARRYING ARTICLES:
It shall be unlawful for any person operating a bicycle to carry a package, bundle or article which prevents the rider from keeping at least one hand upon
the handlebars. (1960 Code)
10-2-19: PARKING:
It shall be unlawful for any person to park a bicycle in such a manner as to interfere or obstruct pedestrian traffic. (1960 Code)
10-2-20: RIDING ON SIDEWALKS:
(A) It shall be unlawful for any person to ride a bicycle upon a sidewalk within a business district.
(B) The clerk is authorized to erect signs on any sidewalk or roadway prohibiting the riding of bicycles thereon, and when such signs are in place it shall be
unlawful for any person to disobey the same. (1960 Code)
10-2-21: LAMPS AND OTHER EQUIPMENT:
(A) Every bicycle when in use at nighttime shall be equipped with a lamp on the front which shall emit a white light visible from a distance of at least five
hundred feet (500') to the front and with a red reflector on the rear of a type which shall be visible from all distances from fifty feet (50') to three hundred
feet (300') to the rear when directly in front of lawful upper beams of headlamps on a motor vehicle. A lamp emitting a red light visible from a distance
of five hundred feet (500') to the rear may be used in addition to the red reflector.
(B) It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a bicycle unless it is equipped with a bell or other device capable of giving a signal audible for a distance
of at least one hundred feet (100'), except that a bicycle shall not be equipped with nor shall any person use upon a bicycle any siren or whistle.
(C) Every bicycle shall be equipped with a brake which will enable the operator to make the braked wheels skid on dry, level, clean pavement. (1960
Code)
Chapter 3
TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES
10-3-1: AUTHORITY TO INSTALL TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES:
The chief of police shall place and maintain traffic control signs, signals and devices when and as required under the traffic regulations of the municipality
to make effective the provisions of said regulations, and may place and maintain such additional traffic control devices as he may deem necessary. (1960
Code)
10-3-2: SPECIFICATIONS FOR TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES:
All traffic control signs, signals and devices shall conform to the approved specifications. All signs and signals required hereunder for a particular purpose
shall so far as practicable be uniform as to type and location throughout the municipality. All traffic control devices so erected and not inconsistent with the
provisions of this title shall be official traffic control devices. (1960 Code)
10-3-3: OBEDIENCE TO OFFICIAL TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES:
The driver of any vehicle shall obey the instructions of any official traffic control device applicable thereto placed in accordance with the traffic regulations
of the municipality, unless otherwise directed by a police officer, subject to the exceptions granted the driver of an authorized emergency vehicle. (1960
Code)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 98/151
10-3-4: WHEN TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES REQUIRED:
No provisions of this title for which signs are required shall be enforced against an alleged violator if at the time and place of the alleged violation an official
sign is not in proper position and sufficiently legible to be seen by an ordinarily observant person. Whenever a particular section does not state that
signsare required, such section shall be effective even though no signs are erected or in place. (1960 Code)
10-3-5: TRAFFIC CONTROL SIGNAL LEGEND:
Whenever traffic is controlled by traffic control signals exhibiting the words "Go", "Caution" or "Stop" or exhibiting different colored lights successively one
at a time or with arrows, the following colors only shall be used and said terms and light shall indicate and apply to drivers of vehicles and pedestrians as
follows: (1960 Code)
(A) Green alone or "Go":
1. Vehicular traffic facing a red light or other stop signal shall stop before entering the crosswalk on the near side of the intersection, or, if none, then
before entering the intersection and shall remain standing until green or "Go" is shown alone, except that after such stop, a right turn shall be
permitted when the same can be executed with safety. (Ord. 284, 10-7-1970)
2. Pedestrians facing the signal may proceed across the roadway within any marked or unmarked crosswalk. (1960 Code)
(B) Yellow alone or "Caution" when following the green or "Go" signal:
1. Vehicular traffic facing the signal is thereby warned that the related green movement is being terminated or that a red indication will be exhibited
immediately thereafter. (Ord. 415, 1-5-1986)
2. Pedestrians facing such signal are thereby advised that there is insufficient time to cross the roadway and any pedestrian then starting to cross shall
yield the right of way to all vehicles.
3. Pedestrians facing such signal shall not enter the roadway until the green or "Go" is shown alone unless authorized to do so by a pedestrian "Walk"
signal.
(C) Red alone or "Stop":
1. Vehicular traffic facing the signal shall stop before entering the crosswalk on the near side of the intersection or, if none, then before entering the
intersection and shall remain standing until green or "Go" is shown alone.
2. No pedestrian facing such signal shall enter the roadway until the green or "Go" is shown alone unless authorized so to do by a pedestrian "Walk"
signal.
(D) Red with green arrow:
1. Vehicular traffic facing such signal may cautiously enter the intersection only to make the movement indicated by such arrowbut shall yield the right
of way to pedestrians lawfully within a crosswalk and to other traffic lawfully using the intersection.
2. No pedestrian facing such signal shall enter the roadway until the green or "Go" is shown alone unless authorized so to do by a pedestrian "Walk"
signal.
(E) In the event an official traffic control signal is erected and maintained at a place other than an intersection, the provisions of this chapter shall be
applicable except as to those provisions which by their nature can have no application. Any stop required shall be made at a sign or marking on the
pavement indicating where the stop shall be made, but in the absence of any such sign or marking the stop shall be made at the signal. (1960 Code)
10-3-6: PEDESTRIAN CONTROL SIGNALS:
Whenever special pedestrian control signals exhibiting the words "Walk" or "Wait" or "Don't walk" are in place such signals shall indicate as follows:
(A) Walk: Pedestrians facing such a signal may proceed across the roadway in the direction of the signal and shall be given the right of way.
(B) Wait Or Don't Walk: It shall be unlawful for any pedestrian to start to cross the roadway in the direction of such signal, but any pedestrian who has
partially completed his crossing on the "Walk" signal shall proceed to a sidewalk or safety zone while the wait signal is showing. (1960 Code)
10-3-7: FLASHING SIGNALS:
Whenever an illuminated flashing red or yellow signal is used in a traffic sign or signal it shall require obedience by vehicular traffic as follows:
(A) Flashing Red (Stop Signal): When a red lens is illuminated with rapid intermittent flashes drivers of vehicles shall stop before entering the nearest
crosswalk at an intersection or at a limit line when marked or, if none, then before entering the intersection and the right to proceed shall be subject to
the rules applicable after making a stop at a stop sign.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 99/151
(B) Flashing Yellow (Caution Signal): When a yellow lens is illuminated with rapid intermittent flashes, drivers of vehicles may proceed through the
intersection or past such signal only with caution.
(C) Railroad Crossings: This section shall not apply at railroad grade crossings. Conduct of drivers of vehicles approaching railroad grade crossings shall
be governed by the rules set forth in chapter 7 of this title. (1960 Code)
10-3-8: DISPLAY OF UNAUTHORIZED SIGNS, SIGNALS OR MARKINGS:
(A) No person shall place, maintain, or display upon or in view of any highway any unauthorized sign, signal, marking, or device which purports to be or is
an imitation of or resembles an official traffic control device or railroad sign or signal, or which attempts to direct the movement of traffic, or which hides
from view or interferes with the effectiveness of traffic, or which hides from view or interferes with the effectiveness of any official traffic control device
or any railroad sign or signal.
(B) No person shall place or maintain nor shall any public authority permit upon any highway any traffic sign or signal bearing thereon any commercial
advertising.
(C) This section shall not be deemed to prohibit the erection upon private property adjacent to highways of signs giving useful directional information and
of a type that cannot be mistaken for official signs.
(D) Every such prohibited sign, signal or marking is hereby declared to be a public nuisance and the authority having jurisdiction over the highway is
hereby empowered to remove the same or cause it to be removed without notice. (1960 Code)
10-3-9: INTERFERENCE WITH OFFICIAL TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES:
It shall be unlawful for any person, without lawful authority, to attempt to or in fact alter, deface, injure, knock down or remove any official traffic control
device or any railroad sign or signal or any inscription, shield or insignia thereon or any part thereof. (1960 Code)
10-3-10: CROSSWALKS AND SAFETY ZONES:
The chief of police is hereby authorized:
(A) To designate and maintain, by appropriate devices, marks or lines upon the surface of the roadway, crosswalks at intersections where in his opinion
there is particular danger to pedestrians crossing the roadway and at such other places as he may deem necessary.
(B) To establish safety zones of such kind and character and at such places as he may deem necessary for the protection of pedestrians. (1960 Code)
10-3-11: TRAFFIC LANES:
(A) The chief of police is hereby authorized to mark traffic lanes upon the roadway of any street or highway where a regular alignment of traffic is
necessary.
(B) Where such traffic lanes have been marked it shall be unlawful for the operator of any vehicle to fail or refuse to keep such vehicle within the
boundaries of such lane except when lawfully passing another vehicle or preparatory to making a lawful turning movement. (1960 Code)
Chapter 4
PARKING REGULATIONS
10-4-1: HOURS PARKING PROHIBITED IN CERTAIN PLACES:
(A) Tyhee Street: No vehicle other than school buses shall be permitted to park along the west side of Tyhee Street between Taylor Street and East Park
Street, between the hours of seven thirty o'clock (7:30) A.M. to three thirty o'clock (3:30) P.M. on any day when any school operated by the
Independent School District 381 shall be in session.
(B) Taylor Street: There shall be a student drop off zone on the south side of Taylor Street beginning at the corner of Taylor Street and Tyhee Street and
then extending in a westerly direction toward Fort Hall Avenue for a distance of one hundred twenty five feet (125'). No vehicle shall be permitted to
park along this section of Taylor Street for any reason other than to make a temporary stop for the sole purpose of dropping off students between the
hours of seven thirty o'clock (7:30) A.M. to three thirty o'clock (3:30) P.M. on any day when any school operated by the Independent School District 381
shall be in session.
(C) Violation An Infraction: Any person violating the provisions of this section shall be deemed guilty of an infraction as set forth under Idaho law. (Ord.
562, 10-16-2002)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 100/151
10-4-2: PARKING PROHIBITED IN CERTAIN PLACES:
(A) Stopping, Standing, Or Parking Prohibited; No Signs Required: It is unlawful for any person to stop, stand, or park a vehicle except when necessary to
avoid conflict with other traffic in compliance with law or the directions of a police officer or traffic control device in any of the following places:
1. On a sidewalk;
2. In front of a public or private driveway;
3. Within an intersection;
4. Within fifteen feet (15') of a fire hydrant;
5. Within twenty feet (20') of a crosswalk at an intersection;
6. Within thirty feet (30') upon the approach of any flashing beacon, stop sign, or traffic control signal located at the side of a roadway;
7. Within fifty feet (50') of the nearest rail of a railroad crossing;
8. Alongside or opposite any street obstruction or excavation when stopping, standing, or parking would obstruct traffic;
9. On a roadway side of any vehicle stopped or parked at the edge of a curb of a street;
10. Upon any bridge or other elevated structure upon a highway or within a highway tunnel;
11. Alongside any curb marked or painted with yellow paint; and
12. Alongside or within any marked bicycle lane which abuts the edge of a public street.
(B) Fort Hall Avenue:
1. It shall be unlawful for any vehicle to park along the southeast curb line of Fort Hall Avenue between its intersection with West Park Street in the city.
2. It shall further be unlawful for any vehicle to park along the northwest curb line of Fort Hall Avenue between its intersection with Howard Street and
Lincoln Avenue.
(C) Bennett Avenue:
1. In order to create a safe and orderly flow of traffic in the vicinity of Hillcrest Grade School, parking of vehicles is hereby prohibited on the south side
of Bennett Avenue from its intersection with Pierce Street to its intersection with Fillmore Street.
2. Further, that same portion of Bennett Avenue shall be prohibited to parking and shall have the use of its right hand lane limited to loading and
unloading of passengers only, as shall be designated by signs and street markings.
3. The north side of that same portion of Bennett Avenue shall be used for angle parking only, as shall be designated by the city.
(D) Pocatello Avenue:
1. Vehicle parking shall be prohibited on the southeast side of Pocatello Avenue from its intersection with Gifford Avenue to its intersection with Hillcrest
Avenue.
(E) Parking In Alley: It is unlawful for any person to park a vehicle within an alley except in the following circumstances: 1) vehicles may be parked in an
alley while actually involved in the loading and unloading of passengers or merchandise, so long as they are parked in a manner or under such
conditions to leave available at least ten feet (10') of width of the alley for the free movement of vehicular traffic when possible and, 2) vehicles may be
parked in an alley upon written permission from the chief of police for exceptional circumstances shown.
(F) Definitions: The term "vehicle" as used in this section shall also include recreational vehicles such as snow machines, motorcycles, golf carts, boats,
campers and motor homes. (Ord. 595, 10-7-2009)
10-4-3: HANDICAPPED PARKING:
(A) No vehicle except a vehicle belonging to a handicapped person, provided further that such vehicle is designated as "handicapped", as per Idaho law,
shall park:
1. Along the west side of Fort Hall Avenue from Idaho Street to the alley from the hours of eleven o'clock (11:00) A.M. to one o'clock (1:00) P.M.,
Mondays, Wednesdays and Fridays. (Ord. 471, 4-6-1994)
2. In the two (2) handicapped parking spaces designated near Hillcrest Elementary School, beginning at the southwest corner of the intersection of
Bennett Avenue and Pierce Street, thence east along the south side of Bennett Avenue a distance of fifty six feet (56'). (Ord. 518, 3-18-1998)
10-4-4: VIOLATIONS OF PARKING REGULATIONS:
Any violations of the parking regulations provided for in this chapter shall be punishable as infractions, pursuant to Idaho law. (Ord. 539, 10-6-1999)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 101/151
Chapter 5
VEHICLE WEIGHT LIMITS; TRUCK ROUTES
10-5-1: WEIGHT LIMIT:
The weight limit for the residential streets of American Falls shall be twenty six thousand (26,000) pounds. (Ord. 552, 12-20-2000)
10-5-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms, phrases, and the derivations shall have the meanings given in this section:
DESTINATION POINT: Any lawful business premises for the loading or unloading of cargo or the final lawful parking place.
DEVIATING TRUCK: A truck that leaves and departs from a truck route while traveling within the city.
OVERSIZED TRUCK OR LOAD: Any truck or load on a truck which would be prohibited on the roads of the state by Idaho Code section 49-1010, or which
may only travel on state roads by permit, pursuant to Idaho Code section 49-1004.
PERSON: A person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company or organization of any kind.
RESIDENTIAL ROUTES: All other streets, avenues, alleys and ways not designated as "truck routes", shall be designated and referred to as "residential
routes".
TRUCK: Any vehicle designed or operated for the purpose of transportation of property, and whose actual vehicle weight exceeds twenty six thousand
(26,000) pounds, and does not include a semitractor, which weighs less than twenty six thousand (26,000) pounds and is separated at the time of
operation from the trailer.
TRUCK ROUTE: A way over certain streets as designated by the city, over and along which trucks (as defined herein) coming into and going out of the city
must operate. (Ord. 552, 12-20-2000)
10-5-3: APPLICATION OF REGULATION:
(A) Trucks: All trucks within the city shall be operated only on the designated truck routes of the city.
(B) Exceptions: This section shall not prohibit:
1. Emergency Vehicles: The operation of emergency vehicles upon any street in the city.
2. Public Utility Trucks: The operation of trucks owned or operated by the city, public utilities, any contractor or materialmen, while engaged in the
repair, maintenance, or construction of streets, street improvements, or street utilities within the city.
3. Detoured Trucks: The operation of trucks upon any officially established detour.
4. Residentially Parked Semitractors: The operation of semitractors on residential streets solely for the purpose of temporarily parking the tractor
portion on private residential property with the permission of the property owner, in compliance with other laws and ordinances.
5. Moving, Service, Delivery Trucks: Trucks that may have occasional use in connection with moving, delivery of goods, or performance of service in a
residential area.
(C) Time Limit: Except as otherwise provided herein, all trucks within the city may be parked on established truck routes for a period not to exceed twenty
four (24) hours, unless special permission is obtained from the chief of police or his designee. Such trucks shall be parked in a manner so as not to
block driveways or other streets or to be a vision hazard for other drivers.
(D) Parking Allowed: Parking is generally permitted on the following streets:
Bannock Avenue from Harrison Street to its intersection with Sunbeam Road.
Falls Avenue from Lincoln Street to McKinley Street.
Fort Hall Avenue from the Highway 39 bypass to Lincoln Street.
Harrison Street.
Idaho Street from Fort Hall Avenue to Highway 39.
Lee Street from Fort Hall Avenue to Whitman Avenue.
Lincoln Street.
McKinley Street from Falls Avenue to Teton Avenue.
North Oregon Trail to Roosevelt Street.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 102/151
Pocatello Avenue.
Roosevelt Street from North Oregon Trail to Bannock Avenue.
Sunbeam Road.
Whitman Avenue.
(E) No Parking Areas: Areas of the truck routes that shall not be used for truck parking are designated as follows:
Bannock Avenue between Roosevelt Street and Sunbeam Road.
Fort Hall Avenue between Lee Street and the Highway 39 bypass.
Fort Hall Avenue between West Park Street and Taylor Street.
McKinley Street between Falls Avenue and city limits.
Pocatello Avenue between Bannock Avenue and city limits.
Sunbeam Road between Bannock Avenue and city limits.
(F) Motors Running: No truck or trailer shall be parked with its motor or refrigeration unit running for more than one-half (1/2) hour. (Ord. 552, 12-20-2000)
10-5-4: ENFORCEMENT:
(A) Clerk Maintains Maps: Accurate maps setting out truck routes designated by the city shall be kept on file in the office of the city clerk and shall be
available to the public.
(B) Street Department To Maintain Signs: The street department shall cause all truck routes upon which truck traffic is required to travel to be clearly
signposted.
(C) Weigh In: The chief of police shall have the authority to require any person driving or in control of any commercial vehicle not proceeding in
accordance with the regulations of this chapter to proceed to any public or private scale available for the purpose of weighing and determining whether
this chapter has been complied with. (Ord. 552, 12-20-2000)
10-5-5: PENALTY:
Other than excepted herein, it is unlawful and shall constitute a misdemeanor for any person to operate a truck at any time upon any residential routes.
(Ord. 552, 12-20-2000)
10-5-6: RESPONSIBILITY FOR DAMAGES:
The owner and the operator of any vehicle or other contrivance over and upon any street, avenue, alley or way within the city shall be jointly and severally
responsible for any and all damages which any of such truck routes or residential routes may sustain as a direct or indirect result of any operation of said
vehicle or other contrivance on any said truck or residential routes in violation of any of the terms or conditions hereof. All said damages may be recovered
by the city in an action at law or equity. (Ord. 552, 12-20-2000)
Chapter 6
SPEED LIMITS
10-6-1: ERECTION OF SIGNS:
The chief of police or other city agent may erect appropriate speed limit signs and school zone signs as deemed necessary to give notice and advise the
general public of the maximum speed limits enacted in this chapter. (Ord. 557, 12-5-2001)
10-6-2: GENERAL SPEED LIMIT:
The speed of twenty five (25) miles per hour is the maximum speed allowed upon any street within the municipality except as otherwise provided in this
title. (Ord. 557, 12-5-2001)
10-6-3: SPEED IN CERTAIN AREAS FIFTY FIVE MILES PER HOUR:
After due consideration of the need therefor, a traffic investigation, and recommendations of the state department of transportation, there is established a
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=458 103/151
maximum speed limit not to exceed fifty five (55) miles per hour as follows:
State Highway 39 within the city limits of American Falls, Idaho. (Ord. 557, 12-5-2001)
10-6-4: SPEED IN CERTAIN AREAS THIRTY MILES PER HOUR:
After due consideration of the need therefor, a traffic investigation, and recommendations of the state department of transportation, there is established a
maximum speed limit not to exceed thirty (30) miles per hour as follows:
Fort Hall Avenue between Harrison and Lee and out to American Falls marina.
Fort Hall Avenue between Lincoln and Harrison.
Harrison Avenue between Fort Hall and Bannock.
Lincoln Street between Teton and Fort Hall.
Pocatello Avenue between Bannock and city limits. (Ord. 557, 12-5-2001)
10-6-5: SPEED IN CERTAIN AREAS TWENTY FIVE MILES PER HOUR:
After due consideration of the need therefor, a traffic investigation, and recommendations of the state department of transportation, there is established a
maximum speed limit not to exceed twenty five (25) miles per hour as follows:
For all other existing streets within or controlled by the city of American Falls unless otherwise designated. (Ord. 557, 12-5-2001)
10-6-6: SCHOOL ZONE SPEED REGULATIONS:
After due consideration of the need therefor, there is established a maximum speed not to exceed twenty five (25) miles per hour in the areas of schools
(school zones) and the speed limit of twenty five (25) miles per hour shall be in effect only Monday through Friday, inclusive, from seven o'clock (7:00)
A.M. until four o'clock (4:00) P.M. from August 25 through June 10 of each year. The twenty five (25) miles per hour school zones are designated as
follows:
Fort Hall between Polk Street and Lincoln Street.
Lincoln Street between Fort Hall Avenue and Teton Street.
Pocatello Avenue between city limits and fifty feet (50') west of Bannock Avenue. (Ord. 557, 12-5-2001)
10-6-7: SPEEDING VIOLATIONS; PENALTIES:
A violation of the speed regulations adopted in this chapter shall constitute an infraction and the penalty therefor shall be as provided in the Idaho
infraction rules as set out in the Idaho Code, adopted July 1, 1983, as amended from time to time, three (3) copies of which are available for use and
examination by the public in the office of the city clerk. (Ord. 557, 12-5-2001)
10-6-8: SEVERABILITY:
Provisions of this chapter are declared to be severable, and if any section, sentence, clause, or phrase of this chapter shall be declared invalid, such
declaration shall not affect the validity of the remaining sections, sentences, clauses, and phrases of this chapter but they shall remain in effect, it being
the intentthat this chapter shall stand notwithstanding the invalidity of any part. (Ord. 557, 12-5-2001)
10-6-9: ESTABLISHMENT:
As established by this chapter, maximum speeds on any street or highway within the city of American Falls and/or within the purview of the city's
jurisdiction are established by an engineering study or traffic investigation, or both, that has been reviewed and approved by an engineer licensed within
the state of Idaho. (Ord. 557, 12-5-2001)
10-6-10: REPEAL OF CONFLICTING CODE PROVISIONS:
Any provision of this code in conflict with the provisions set forth in this chapter is repealed and of no force or effect. (Ord. 557, 12-5-2001)
